mass movement with which he identi 
fies himself. 
20. Notice the masochistic tendency of 
leftist tactics. Leftists protest by lying 
down in front of vehitles, they inten- 
tionally provoke police or racists to 
abuse them, etc. These tactics may 
often be effective, but many leftists use 
them not as a meansto an end but 
because they PREFER masochistic tac- 
ties. Self-hatred is aleftist trait. 
21. Leftists may claim that their 
activism is motivated by compassion or 
by moral principles,and moral princi- 
ple does play a role for the leftist of the 
oversocialized type. But compassion 
and moral principle cannot be the main 
motives for leftist activism. Hostility is 
too prominent a component of leftist 
behavior; so is the drive for power. 
Moreover, much leftist behavior is not 
rationally calculated to be of benefit to 
the people whom the leftists claim to be 
trying to help. For example, if one 
believes that affirmative action is good 
for black people, does it make sense to 
demand affirmative action in hostile or 
dogmatic terms? Obviously it would be 
more productive to take a diplomatic 
and conciliatory approach that would 
make at least verbal and symbolic con- 
cessions to white people who think that 
affirmative action discriminates 
against them. But leftist activists do 
not take such an approach because it 
would not satisfy their emotional 
needs. Helping black people is not their 
real goal. Instead, rice problems serve 
as an excuse for them to express their 
own hostility and frustrated need for 
power. In doing sothey actually harm 
black people, because the activists’ hos- 
tile attitude toward the white majority 
tends to intensify race hatred. 
22. If our society had no social prob- 
lems at all, the leftists would have to 
INVENT problems in order to provide 
themselves with an excuse for making 
a fuss. 
23. We emphasize that the foregoing 
does not pretend to he an accurate 
description of everyone who might be 
considered a leftist. It is only a rough 
indication of a general tendency of left- 
ism. 


OVERSOCIALIZATION 


24. Psychologists use the term “social- 
ization” to designate the process by 
which children are trained to think 
and act as society demands. A person is 
said to be well socialized if he believes 
in and obeys the moral code of his soci- 
ety and fits in well as a functioning 
part of that society, It may seem sense- 
less to say that many leftists are over- 
socialized, since the leftist is perceived 
as a rebel. Nevertheless, the position 
can be defended. Many leftists are not 
such rebels as they seem. 

25. The moral code of our society is so 
demanding that no one can think, feel 
and act in a completely moral way. For 


example, we are not supposed to hate 
anyone, yet almost everyone hates 
somebody at some time or other, 
whether he admits it to himself or not 
Some people are 50 highly socialized 
that the attempt to think, feel and act 
morally imposes a severe burden on 
them. In order to avoid feelings of guilt, 
they continually have to deceive them 
selves about their own motives and 
find moral explanations for feelings 
and actions that in reality have a non 
moral origin. We use the term "overso- 
cialized” to deserihe such people. (2) 

26. Oversocialization can lead to low 
self-esteem, a sense of powerlessness. 
defeatism, guilt, ete. One of the most 
important means by which our society 
Socializes children is by making them 
feel ashamed of behavior or speech that 
is contrary to society's expectations. If 
this is overdone, or if a particular child 
is especially susceptible to such feel- 
ings, he ends by feeling ashamed of 
HIMSELF. Moreover the thought and 
the behavior of the oversocialized per. 
Son are more restricted by society's 
expectations than are those of the light- 
ly socialized person, The majority of 
people engage in a significant amount 
of naughty behavior. They lie, they 
commit petty thefts, they break traffic 
laws, they goof off at work, they hate 
Someone, they say spiteful things or 
they use some underhanded trick to get 
ahead of the other guy. The oversocial. 
ized person cannot do these things, or 
if he does do them he generates in him- 
Self a sense of shame and selthatred. 
‘The oversocialized person cannot even 
experience, without guilt, thoughts or 
feelings that are contrary to the accept- 
ed morality; he cannot think “unclean” 
thoughts. And socialization is not just a 
matter of morality; we are socialized to 
conform to many norms of behavior 
that do not fall under the heading of 
morality. Thus the oversocialized per: 
son is kept on a psychological leash 
and spends his life running on rails 
that society has laid down for him. In 


c among 
the more serious cruelties that human 


28. The leftist of ersocialized type: 
tries to get om tus pave 


‘his psychological leash 
and assert his autonomy Sy Tebening 
But usually he is not strong enough to 
rebel against the most basic values of 
Generally speaking, the goals 
y's leftists are NOT in conflict 
with the accepted morality. On the con- 
trary, the left takes an accepted moral 
principle, adopts it as its own, and then 
accuses mainstream society of violat- 
ing that principle. Examples: racial 
equality, equality of the sexes, helping 
Poor people, peace as opposed to war, 
nonviolence generally, freedom of 
expression, kindness to animals. More 
fundamentally, the duty of the individ- 
ual to serve society and the duty of 
society to take care of the individual, 
All these have been deeply rooted val- 
ues of our society (or at least of its mid- 
dle and upper classes [4] for a long 
time. These values are explicitly or 
implicitly expressed or presupposed in 
most of the material presented to us by 
the mainstream communications 
media and the educational system. 
Leftists, especially those of the overso- 
cialized type, usually do not rebel 
against these principles but justify 
their hostility to society by claiming 
(with some degree of truth) that society 
is not living up to these principles. 

29. Here is an illustration of the way in 
which the oversocialized leftist shows 
his real attachment to the conventional 
attitudes of our society while pretend- 
ing to be in rebellion against it. Many 
leftists push for affirmative action, for 
moving black people into high-prestige 
jobs, for improved education in black 
schools and more money for such 
schools; the way of life of the black 
“underclass” they regard as a social 
disgrace. They want to integrate the 
black man into the system, make him a 
business executive, a lawyer, a scien- 
tist just like upper-middle-class white 
people. The leftists will reply that the 
last thing they want is to make the 
black man into a copy of the white 
man; instead, they want to preserve 
African American culture. But in what 
does this preservation of African 
American culture consist? It can hard- 
ly consist in anything more than eating 
black-style food, listening to black-style 
music, wearing black-style clothing 
and going to a black-style church or 
mosque. In other words, it can express 
itself only in superficial matters. In all 
ESSENTIAL respects most leftists of 
the oversocialized type want to make 
the black man conform to white, mid- 
die-class ideals, They want to make 
him study technical subjects, become 
an executive or a scientist, spend his 
life climbing the status ladder to prove 
that black people are as good as white. 
‘They want to make black fathers 
“responsible,” they want black gangs to 
become nonviolent, etc. But these are 
exactly the values of the industrial- 
technological system. The system 
couldn't care less what kind of music a 
man listens to, what kind of clothes he 
wears or what religion he believes in 
as long as he studies in school, holds a 


ete 


pace 


respectable job, climbs the status lad 
der, is a “responsible” parent, is nonve 
olent and so forth. In effect, however 
much he.may deny it, the oversocial 
ized leftist wants to integrate the black 
man into the system and make him 
adopt its values. 
30. We certairily do not claim that left 
ists, even of the oversocialized type, 
NEVER rebel against the fundamental 
values of our society. Clearly they 
sometimes do. Some oversocialized left 
ists have gone so far as to rebel against 
one of modern society's most impor 
principles by engaging in physical vie 
lence. By their own account, violence is 
for them a form of “liberation.” In 
other words, by committing violence 
they break through the psycholo; 
restraints that have been trained 
them. Because they are oversocialized 
these restraints have been more confin 
ing for them than for others; hence 
their need to break free of them. Hut 
they usually justify their rebellion in 
terms of mainstream values. If they 
engage in violence they claim to be 
fighting against racism or the like. 
41. We realize that many objections 
could be raised to the foregoing thumb- 
nail sketch of leftist psychology. The 
rea) situation is complex, and anyti 
like a complete dese Tiption of it wo 
take several volumes even if the neces. 
sary data were available. We claim 
only to have indicated very roughly the 
two most important tendencies in the 
psychology of modern leftism. 
32. The problems of the leftist are 
indicative of the problems of our soci 
ety 45 a Whole. Low self-esteem, de: 
sive tendencies and defeatism are nat 
restricted to the left. Though they are 
especially noticeable in the left, they 
are widespread in our society. And 
today’s society tries to socialize us to a 
greater extent (han any pre soci 
ety. We are even told by experts haw to 
eat, how to exercise, how to make love, 
how to raise our kids and so forth 


THE POWER PROCESS 


33. Human beings have a need (proba- 
bly based in biology) for something 
that we will call the * power process.”” 
This is closely related to the need for 
power (which is widely recognized) but 
is not quite the same thing. The power 
Process has four elements. The three 
most clear-cut of these we call goal, 
effort and attainment of goal 
(Everyone needs to have goals whose 
attainment requires effort, and needs 
to succeed in attaining at least some of 
his goals.) The fourth element is more 
eet to define and may not be neces- 
sary for everyone. We call i 
spawn ae neand later ene cots ah 
4 Consider the hypothetical case of a 
man who can have anything he wants 
just by wishing for it. Such a man has 
power, but he will develop serious psy- 
chological problems, At first he will 
have a lot of fun, but by and by he wi 
become acutely bored and demoralized 
Eventually he may become clinically 
depressed. History shows that leisure 
aristocracies tend to become decadent 
This is not true of fighting aristocra. 
cies that have to struggle to maintain 
their power. But leisured, secure aris- 
tocracies that have no need to exert 
themselves usually become bored, 
hedonistic and demoralized, even 
though they have power. This shows 
that power is not enough. One must 
have goals toward which to exercise 
one’s power. 
35, Everyone has goals; if nothing else, 
to obtain the physical necessities of 
life: food, water and whatever clothing 
and shelter are made necessary by the 
climate. But the leisured aristocrat 
obtains these things without effort. 
Hence his boredom and demoraliza- 
tion. 
36. Nonattainment of important goals 
results in death if the goals are physi- 
ca] necessities, and in frustration if 
nonattainment of the goals is compati: 
ble with survival. Consistent failure to 
attain goals throughout life results in 
defeatism, low self-esteem or depres- 
sion. 
37, Thus, in order to avoid serious psy 
chological problems, a human being 
needs goals whose attainment juires 
effort, and he must have a reasonable 
rate of success in attaining his goals. 


SURROGATE ACTIVITIES 


38, But not every leisured aristocrat 
becomes bored and demoralized. For 
example, the emperor Hirohito, instead 
of sinking into decadent hedonism, 
devoted himself to marine biology, a 


field in which he became distinguished. 


When people do not have to exert them: 
selves to satisfy their physical needs 
they often set up artificial goals for 
themselves: In many cases they then 
pursue these goals with the same ener- 
gy and emotional involvement that 
they otherwise would have put into the 
search for physical necessities. Thus 
the aristocrats of the Roman Empire 
had their literary pretensions; many 
European aristocrats a few centuries 
ago invested tremendous time and 
energy in hunting, though they certain: 
ly didn’t need the meat; other aristocra: 
cies have competed for status through 
elaborate displays of wealth; and a few 
aristocrats, like Hirohito, have turned 
to science. 

39. We use the term “surrogate activi 
ty” to designate an activity that is 
directed toward an artificial goal that 
people set up for themselves merely in 
order to have some goal to work 
toward, or let us say, merely for the 
sake of the “fulfillment” that they get 


sos Beene meme og 


— 


172. First let us postulate that the computer scientists succeed in develop- 
ing intelligent machines that can do all things better than human beings 
can do them. In that case presumably all work will be done by vast, high- 


ly-organized systems of machines and no human effort will be necessary... 


173. ...If the machines are permitted to make all their own decisions, we 
can’t make any conjectures as to the results, because it is impossible to 
guess how such machines might behave. We only point out that the fate of 
the human race would be at the mercy of the machines. It might be ar- 
gued that the human race would never be foolish enough to hand over all 
the power to the machines. But we are suggesting neither that the human 
race would voluntarily turn power over to the machines nor that the ma- 
chines would willfully seize power. What we do suggest is that the human 
race might easily permit itself to drift into a position of such dependence 
on the machines that it would have no practical choice but to accept all of 
the machines’ decisions. As society and the problems that face it become 
more and more complex and machines become more and more intelligent, 
people will let machines make more of their decisions for them, simply 
because machines-made decisions will bring better results than man-made 
ones. Eventually a stage may be reached at which the decisions necessary 
to keep the system running will be so complex that human beings will be 
incapable of making them intelligently. At that stage the machines will 

be in effective control. People won’t be able to just shut the machines off, 
because they will be so dependent on them that turning them off would 


amount to suicide. 


174. On the other hand it is possible that human control over the ma- 
chines may be retained. In that case the average man may have control 
over certain private machines of his own, such as his care or his personal 
computer, but control over large systems of machines will be in the hands 


of a tiny elite...

FBI behaviorists were at a loss 
to explain the Unabomber’s motives 
until after the April 19 bombing’ of a 
federal building in Oklahoma.City. 
On April 20, the bomber broke years 
of silence by mailing four letters:that 
began to detail his social philosophy. 
Criminologists theorized the bomber 
felt upstaged by the blast. 

His communications culminated 


‘in June, when he mailed the Times 


and the Post his 56-page text,-plus 
11 pages of footnotes and other: ma- 
terial. FBI agents began circulating 
the manifesto among professors to 
see if they recognized it as the work 
of a former student. Much of the fo- 
eus concentrated on the Chicago 
area, where the Unabomber’s first 
bomb was found in a parking lot at 
the University of Illinois Chicago 
Circle campus. ‘ 

In recent weeks, agents also have 
interviewed high school teachers in 
the Chicago area in the belief, that 
the Unabomber spent his early 
years there. Members of the task 
foree have theorized that the Una- 
bomber attended or spent time 
around Northwestern University, 
the University of Illinois, the Uni- 
versity of Utah, Brigham Young 
University and the University of 
California at Berkeley. oe 

More than 20,000 calls have 
swamped the Unabomber hot ‘line. 
At least 90 agents are working full- 
time to track down leads in a man- 
hunt Freeman called “unprecedent- 
ed in law enforcement.” Three agen- 
cies are working together: eer

eventually bear fruit,” he said.“T?m

POLITICAL CORRECTNESS 
AND “LEFTISM” 


When we speak of leftists in this 
article we have in mind mainly so- 
cialists, collectivists, “Politically cor- 
rect” types, feminists, gay and dis- 
ability activists, animal-rights activ- 
ists and the like. . .. The two psycho- 
logical tendencies that underlie mod- 
ern leftism we call feelings of inferi- 
ority and oversocialization. Feelings 
of inferiority are characteristic of 
modern leftism as a whole, while 
oversocialization is characteristic 
only of a certain segment of modern 
leftism; but this segment is highly 
influential. ... 

Political correctness has its 
stronghold among university profes- 
sors, who have secure employment 
with comfortable salaries, and the 
majority of whom are heterosexual 
white males from middle to upper 
middle-class families. 

Many leftists have an intense 
identification with the problems of 
groups that have an image of being 
weaale fxramoan) defeated (American 


to over- It 


22h DULY Uae 


do see these groups as inferior that — 
they identify with their problems. 
FREEDOM OF THE PRESS 
As for our constitutional rights, 
consider for example that of freedom 
of the press. We certainly don’t 
mean to knock that right; it is a very 
important tool for limiting concen- 
tration of political power and for 
Keeping those who do have political 
power in line by publicly exposing 
any misbehavior on their part. But 
freedom of the press is of very little 
use to the average citizen as an indi 
vidual. The mass media are most! 
under the control of large organi, 
tions that are integrated into the 
system. Anyone who has a little 
“money can have something printed, 
or can distribute it on the Internet 
or in some such way, but what he has 
to say will be swamped by the vast 
volume of material put out by the 
media, hence it will have no practical 
effect. 
To make an impression on soci- 
ety with words is therefore almost 
impossible for most individuals and 
small groups. Take us (FC) for ex- 
ample. If we had never done any- 
thing violent and had submitted the 
present writings to a publisher, they 
probably would not have been ac- 
cepted. If they had been accepted 
and published, they probably would

ASSOCIATED PRESS 


NEW YORK - Journalists will 
argue for years about the agonizing 
decision by The New York Times 
and The Washington Post to publish 
the 35,000-word manifesto of the ter- 
rorist known as the Unabomber. 

In the din of debate yesterday, 
though, there was one patch of 
agreement. Editors around the coun- 
try shared a sense of relief that they 
were not the ones on the hot seat. 

“I’m glad, as most editors in the 
country are, that it wasn’t my deci- 
sion to make,” said Sandra Mims 
Rowe, editor of The Oregonian in 
Portland. She added: “I think they 
made the right decision.” 

“T instinctively oppose it,” said 
Doug Clifton, executive editor of The 
Miami Herald. Still, he added, “it’s a 


heck of a lot easier to say that in the 
abstract.” Les 

In the theoretical debate, ithe 
lines were drawn between those who 


said the two newspapers were acting 
in the public interest, and those-who 


said the Times and Post had sacri- 
ficed journalistic independence-and 
set a dangerous precedent by eaving 
in to a killer. The publishers of the 
newspapers, Donald Graham of the 
Post and Arthur Sulzberger Jr. of 
the Times, said they had agreed to 
print the manifesto at the urging of 
Attorney General Janet Reno.and 
FBI Director Louis Freeh. 
John Seigenthaler, who heads a 
news industry think tank in Nash- 
ville, The Freedom Forum First 
Amendment Center, called the deci- 
sion “a sad precedent” that was, yn- 
avoidable under the circumstanees.

Michael Rustigan, a criminologist at San 
Francisco State University who has tracked 
the Unabomber’s career, calls such thinking 
“naive utopianism.”. 

Although such romanticism is shared by 
some ~ including 19th-century French phi- 


losopher Jean Jacques Rousseau, as well as 
young anarchists who live on the streets of 
the Haight in San Francisco - Rustigan 
says most anthropologists agree that life in 
the village was actually more stifling than 
modern life because of its ey os 


It is such intolerance, Rustigan ; 
that led the Unabomber to his self-de- 
scribed tedious life of bomb-making. Rusti- 
gan imagines that the bomber may ope 
have aspired to becoming a university 
fessor who could mesmerize and sway 
students, but balked at the eco-dimtidstifig 
prospect of working his way up through the 
university hierarchy. OT QUITE 7 

Instead he turned to violence. “He's got 
an alterative career, and the whole nation is 
listening to him,” Rustigan says. 

Should we be listening? Andy Caffrey, a 
10-year member of the radical environmen- la 
tal movement called Earth First!, says his 
movement has been trying for years with- 

- out much success to make some of the sathe 
points as the Unabomber. Like the bomber, 
Earth First! followers believe in promoting 
small-scale sustainable enterprise and feel . 
that most members of society are so cut off nO 
from nature that they don’t realize the dan- 

ger the planet is in. 

“There is a huge need for society to al- 
low these ideas to circulate freely,” C: 
says. “It seems that, so far, nonviolent 
grass-roots organizations have not succeed- 
ed, and along comes this guy with his 
bombs and people pay attention. To me, it’s 
kind of scary.” 

Paul Saffo, a director at The Insti 
for the Future, a 26-year-old:nonprofit 
search foundation in Menlo Park, Calif., 
counts the Unabomber’s message. - 
technology sentiment, he says, is a classic 
example of the kind of jumpiness brought 
on by the end of centuries. “The Una- 
bomber is simply a menace,” Saffo says, ai'-

Unapack, TOP TEN REASONS TO VOTE UNABOMBER (essential campaign literature) 
NB: Widely reproduced in zines, subculture papers, incl. CoE’s ‘Snuff It #3’ 


TOP TEN REASONS TO VOTE UNABOMBER 
Your presidential write-in choice for ’96 
by Lydia Eccles 


THE BOYS. Clinton, Gingrich, Powell, Perot, Forbes, 
Dole, Gramm, Lugar, Alexander, Dornan, Keyes, etc. 
HE'S HOT. His favorability ratings may be low, but his 
name recognition is close to 100%. We won't need to 
hype him—he’s already hyped. A Unabomber write-in 
campaign can surf the media wave. He’s the perfect imposter 
to undermine the presidential election process as it unfolds, 
and turn the fraudulent election process against itself. 

THE VISION THING. “The Industrial Revolution and its 

consequences have been a disaster for the human race.” 
Regardless of what you think of the Unabomber and his 
analysis, the right issues are finally raised. Can you even 
conceive of any legitimate candidacy, election, or debate 
which will allow the real questions to be put on the table? We 
need to dish them out before they cool off. . . They’re giving 
an election, but we can crash it and have our own referendum 
on corpo-technocracy. If the Unabomber put a hairline crack 
in the myth of progress, we should apply a wedge now—the 
Unabomber’s fifteen seconds are just about up. But an 
election lasts a year. An anti-technological rallying point only 
came into being because of the criminal chase. There’s not 
going to be another opportunity. 

CRASH THE PARTIES. The election offers a “choice” once 

all the real decisions have been made. On top of being 
an anti-republicrat vote, the Unabomber campaign is a 
counterfoil to faux “populist” outsider-insiders like business 
magnate Ross Perot and Gulf warrior Colin Powell (a.k.a. the 
military-industrial complex.) The third party “alternative” is 
designed to safely channel voter alienation into a centrist, 
media-sanctioned agenda and immunize the system against real 
change. 

IF ELECTED HE WILL NOT SERVE. 

president vote. He’s not running, so this can be a 
bottom-up free-for-all campaign. Campaign literature, 
posters, sound bytes, platforms, pranks, the rest: have it your 
way. 
6] DON’T WASTE YOUR VOTE. The media’s like a 

psychiatrist—and you can’t NOT communicate in an 
election. If you boycott the polls, you'll be counted as 
apathetic, complacent, or still worse, contented. If you vote 
for the mainstream lesser of evils, who don’t actually 
represent your views, you’ ve affirmed the political system and 
buried your voice. Either way you've wasted your vote. To 
vote for the Unabomber is to vote and boycott at the same 
time. If nothing else, it’s a vote against the election charade. 
It can be only seen as absolute protest, ridicule, or a “none-of- 
the-above” spurning of the political menu. You can cast an 
anarchistic vote you feel good about, and send the message 
that the presidential elections are a fraud. And you can still 
vote in local races and referendums where your vote counts 
for something. 
VOTE AGAINST THE PROPAGANDA MACHINE. The 

Unabomber did an end run around the media monopoly, 
and published without editorial clearance. The Unabomber 
has, by the magnitude of his plan, exposed the media as a 
closed communications system, making it very clear—in case 
anyone hadn’t noticed—that it’s a communications war. Mass 
media are launched from a heavily-secured fortress. Other 
terrorists seek publicity as a means to other ends. The 


It’s a nobody-for- 


Unabomber used terrorism to gain publicity as an end in itself. 
Notice how the press seeks to channel interpretation of the 
Unabomber story, covering it as a serial-killer story of crime 
and insanity, while excluding consideration of the ideas 
themselves. They would have us believe that it would be 
disastrous if media weren’t controlled from the top. Op-ed 
pages resounded with journalists lamenting, “Why didn’t he 
have to get editorial approval? What if copy cats are aroused, 
crazies who actually want access to the media, rather than 
simply being passive target markets for political and 
commercial propaganda?” Imagine mass communications not 
subject to corporate control. People might say anything... 
even things not “fit to print.” Exactly. When ABC Nightly 
News gets renamed Disney World, you'll cherish the memory 
of your Unabomber vote. 

HE'S GOT THE CREDENTIALS. The Unabomber’s use of 

violence should not disqualify him from consideration. 
His willingness and ability to effectively use violence to 
achieve strategic political goals merely demonstrate the 
essential qualifications to be president. After all, Colin 
Powell’s ONLY qualification is his performance as an 
effective killer. No one’s called him a serial killer, or said he 
craved attention. No running candidate has condemned the 
Gulf War genocide. This is a country that played war like a 
video game in a high-tech funhouse. We aren’t even allowed 
information as to how many Iraqis, civilian or military, our 
tax dollars blew away. That Bill Clinton avoided the draft and 
hadn’t killed was considered a lack of qualifications. Luckily 
he picked up points for presiding over numerous executions in 
his home state of Arkansas. Occupational deaths and diseases 
. . . Violence? Cancer deaths caused by toxins in the air, in 
food, and workplaces . . . Violence? A minimuin wage that 
is half the poverty level, with the hunger, stress, disease and 
early death that ensue . . . Violence? The media just finished 
re-claborating the rationale for bombing Hiroshima and 
Nagasaki ... Violence? Terror? Anyone bringing up 
violence should put it all on the table, not just select attacks on 
the power structure. Anyone who can truly take a stand 
against violence in any form—and that would include the 
American Revolution—can say the Unabomber shouldn’t be 
president on that basis. But he’s not running anyway, and 
even a landslide wouldn’t actually put him in office. That’s 
the beauty of voting for a fugitive from the law. 
9 | ENTERTAINMENT VALUE. Watch your favorite TV pundits 

try to swallow, digest and regurgitate a Unabomber 
constituency. It’s a message that can’t be neutralized or 
explained away. The most minimal Unabomber returns would 
disrupt the usual discussion of false problems and false 
solutions (usually known as “reform.”) 

DON'T BLAME ME-I VOTED FOR THE UNABOMBER. You 
can sport your bumper sticker after the election . . . but 

not on a Car! 


The player who trespasses against the 
rules or ignores them is a “spoil sport.” 
The spoil sport shatters the play-world 
itself. By withdrawing from the game, he 
reveals the relativity and fragility of the 
play world. He robs play of its illusions.

| INDIA (S96 
Ask a few questions here and there, but do it casually. 


THE POLITICS OF DAILY LIFE 


Think of your direct bodily experience of life. 
No one can lie to you about that. 


Do you hear insect sound of drones clickering keyboards 
in a fluorescent hive of fabric-padded cubicles? 

How many hours a day do you spend in front of a TV screen? 
A computer screen? An automobile screen? All three screens 
combined? Is software your supervisor? 

And how many hours a day do you sleep? 

How are you affected by sound? 

How are you affected by light? 

How are you affected by warmth and touch? 
How are you affected by music? 

Is a good record better than live music raw? 
ls it simply sound you want? Or shared ritual magic? 
How many of your rituals come at you through a glass, 
vicariously? 

What are you being screened from? 

Does it bother you if the windows don't open, 
and even your air is "conditioned"? 

How about your degree and variety of body movement? 
How do you feel in situations of enforced passivity? 

How are you affected by a non-stop assault of symbolic 
communication, audio, robotic voices video, print, billboard, 
as you stumble through the forest of signs? 

What are they urging upon you? 

Do you need contemplation? Do you remember it? 
Thinking from inside, rather than reacting to stimuli? 
ls it hard to look away? 

Is looking in the very thing that cannot be permitted? 
How are you affected by being in crowds? 

How much bodily space do you need? 

Do you find yourself blocking 
your empathetic responses to other humans? 

Do you find yourself committing acts of symbolic violence? 
How are you affected by.the size of the room you're in? 
By living in two and three dimensional grids? 


And by the visual space? Do you need to see the sky? Water? 
Foliage? Animals? Glinting, glimmering, moving? 
(Is that why you have a pet, an aquarium, and fernplants?}) 

Or is video your glinting, glimmering, moving? 
Who prepares your meals? Do you eat standing up? 
Do you trust what you're eating? 

How are you affected by standardized time, 
designed solely to synchronize your movements with those of 
millions of others? How long do you ever go without knowing 

what time it is? Who or what controls your minutes and hours? 

The minutes and hours that add up to your life? 
How are you affected by being moved around 
without control, in elevators, subways, escalators, conveyor belts? 
How are you affected by waiting? 

waiting in line, waiting in traffic, waiting to pee, waiting...learning 

to discipline and punish your spontaneous urge? 

How are you affected by being immobilized and scheduled 
rather than wandering and roaming freely and spontaneously? 
Scavenging? (Shoplifting?) 

Can you use your hands creatively, 
building making touching a variety of materials? 

How are you affected by holding in your desires? 

By sexual repression, by the delay or denial of pleasure, 
starting in childhood, along supression of everything in you that 
evidences your wild nature, your animal life? 
is pleasure dangerous? is danger joy? 

What are we deprived of by labor- saving devices? 

And thoughi- saving devices? 

How are you affected by the efficiency requirement that puts the 
end product ahead of the process, that values only the future 
and never the moment, the present moment that gets shorter 
and shorter, as we try to speed to the future endpoint? 

Are you saving time? 

Are you lonely in a way that language can't allay 
or even express? 

Do you sometimes feel yourself ready to 


LOSE CONTROL? 


That had been the signal. 


Above & Opposite: 
May 1996 
Lydia Eccles, The Politics Of Daily Life 


Ted Kaczynski is arrested in his cabin near Lincoln, Montana 


NB: He had lived there for 25 years

WRITE-IN 
FOR PRESIDENT 


WSO MLR 96 


All you have to lose is the political illusion... 


ARE YOU READY FOR THE RUPTURE? 


The Unabomber Presidential Write-In Campaign formally launched its candidacy 
today, April 4th, 1996. Unapack, the Unabomber political action group, has already 
been engaged in preliminary campaign activities to assess the candidate's potential 
strengths and weaknesses, primarily in New England, where it was visible and active in 
both the New Hampshire and Massachusetts primaries. The Unabomber 
communicated to the FblI via family members that he was ready to emerge, sending an 
unmistakeable signal to Unapack that he is ready, willing and fully-committed to 
enduring the siress of a no-holds barred presidential run, and is even willing to submit to 
a lenthy trial and possible life sentence to do so. To stress the "Wild Nature" theme of 
the campaign, the candidate timed his announcement to coincide with a lunar 
eclipse— a red moon seen only in Massachusetts—the home-base of Unapack, and also 
of his alma mater, Harvard University. The Unapack campaign urges voters to “Leave 
Politics Behind..." and awaken from the technological trance. “Each Unabomber vote 
cast will contribute to opening up communication about the ends, ideals, and goals 
of our civilization,” states Unapack literature. The campaign has sparked interest from 
voters nationwide, and has generated press stories not only in the US, but also in 


Canada and abroad. The campaign has been endorsements to date include SEX-POL. 
and the Debtor's Union.

debates protesting the systematic suppression and exclusion of non-mainsiream 
candidates by the media, in collaboration with well-funded candidates who purchase 
advenising time. The press-sponsored debate excludes both the Libertarian candidate, 
George Phillee, and the Conservative candidate, Steve Gallagher.

How's things? 
> 
Things is fascinating and fast. We just had a run-in with Time-Warner 
about a television piece they tried to produce about us which they dumped 
after shooting because they were so angry about our interfering with the 
simulation they had attempted to stage. Their ostensible reason was 
their concern with our "credibility"---Unapack? Credibility? Nice for 
them to be concerned! They were extremely hostile and rude during the 
shoot because (1) Chris was in drag, ag he always is in public, and (2) 
we documented the process. Of course no one involved in the production 
had even glanced at material about us. Instead their research department 
just saw an opportunity to do yet another "Why does the Unabomber have a 
following among computer geeks" story, which suits their ends because 
they get to say that any Unabomber following inherently lacks credibility 
by being on the internet at all. (The question of the use of technology 
in an attack upon technological ideology is supposed to be the trump 
card that wins the trick--) This campaign is turning into a case 
study in press process, which is appropriate considering the candidate, and 
which 
incidentally is truly beginning to justify, in my mind, the extremes that he 
went to. 
If you have any thoughts on this, (diffuse censorship, through structural 
arrangements, as opposed to through actually changing stories after 
they're written) we're basically opening up a forum (a kind of 
Journalists Anonymous) for é 
examining the position of journalists as tools, willing or unwilling, of 
Management layers that in turn can serve only corporate ends, i.e. 
pursuit of power. (Then you get to the same survival game between 
corporations--"Real performance means total control!" Nynex, Atlantic 
Bell, AT&T, etc.) It seems there are fewer and fewer winners in this 
game, once you start to trace the S&M pecking order. Maybe none. 
The upper ups get their long weekends. Conspiracy is unneccesary. It just 
becomes an ideology of conquest and hierarchy using humans as a reproduction 
process. 


Overt 
censorship seems actually to signal the failure of 
prior, higher level preventive censorship by market research 
and considerations (commodification of speech), division of labor, 
and format/production values, and the creation of a workforce 
of alienated journalists through 
destructign of their daily lives which are a precondition to maintaining

Not a month has passed since’ 


his arrest, but Unabomber sus- 
pect Theodore J. Kaczynski has 
already arrived at that peculiar 
intersection in American culture 
where infamy turns to celebrity. 

A published edition of the 
Unabomber’s 35,000-word mani- 
festo has sold out at many Bay 
Area stores. Kaczynski and the 
Unabomber have been regular 
subjects of Jay Leno’s late-night 
comedy skits. Their exploits are 


discussed on hundreds of Inter- 
net sites. At one site viewers can 
buy a Unabomber T-shirt, as if 
he were a rock star; another site 
is promoting him as a write-in 
candidate for president. 

While federal agents assem- 
ble their case against Kaczynski 


and prosecutors ponder whether - 


to seek the death penalty, Ameri- 
cans seem to have an interest 
verging on fascination for the 
Montana hermit believed re- 
sponsible for three deaths and 23

UNABOMBER: Mythic Status 


From Pagel 
_ injuries during a 17-year campaign 
of terror. 

Perhaps it is the inevitable cu- 
riosity summoned by one of the 
most bizarre and unnerving 
crimes of the century. But crimi- 
nologists, writers, psychiatrists 
-and scholars suggest that the inter- 
est is far more complex — and that 
it reveals much about Americans’ 
ingrained respect for rugged indi- 
vidualism and our concern about 
runaway technology. 

“The Unabomber developed a 
degree of notoriety — he’s almost 
a folk hero — because he was able 
to elude police for so many years,” 
says Eric Hickey, a criminology 
professor at California State Uni- 
versity at Fresno who worked with 
the FBI during its long probe. 

“There’s also a degree of sym- 
pathy, absolutely. Not just people 
who are poor, but at*all socioeco- 
nomic levels. These people don’t 
feel they’re part of society. They 
might think, ‘He shouldn’t have 


story packs the existential shock 


and high moral struggle of Fyodor 
Dostoyevsky’s “Crime and Punish- 
ment.” 

The Unabomber story took 
time to build momentum and de- 
velop its characters, but since 1993, 
one climax has followed another. 

Two professors injured, an ad- 
vertising executive and a timber 


industry lobbyist killed. A threat. 


to blow up a jetliner — the bomb- 
er’s little joke. The FBI rendered 
helpless, even as agents mounted 
the most sophisticated manhunt in 
US. history. 

The audience watched raptly. 
The Unabomber, like a comic book 
super-villain, seemed to be a crimi- 
nal genius at the top of his form. 

When Kaczynski was arrested 


April 3, the story only got more in- . 


teresting. The main character in 
the drama was full of contradic- 
tions. 

A lonely genius, painfully shy. 
A brilliant mathematician and a 
natural-born bomb-maker. An un- 


resents the opposite of those traits.

For immediate release: May 28, 1996 


Picture: Unabomber Campaign billboard, Stuart Street, Boston (Adjacent to ValuJet 
billboard) 


UNABOMBER ‘96 CAMPAIGN LAUNCHES 
POSITIVE OUTDOOR AD CAMPAIGN 


The Unabomber'9?é Campaign unveiled a new outdoor advertising campaign 
which shows its committment to upbeat, positive advertising, in an electoral race 
characterized by personal attacks and character bashing. Unapack’s low-tech, low- 
budget black and white graphics employ clip-art to stress the priorities of the 
campaign. Unapack ads will target passerbys who will relate to the standardized 
human icon as well as thinking, that looks totally cheap! | could have done better 
myself! In contrast, Bob Dole has spent 37 million enriching advertising and media 
industries by producing slick television advertisements designed to keep him moving to 
the right faster than Bill Clinton. Unapack has ruled out television as an advertising 
medium because it would send the wrong message to add to network profits. “And 
why should we pay when there is already so much free advertising for Unabomber '96? 
Beyond the newscasts themselves, which daily affirm our campaign themes, every 
Official “bad air day” announcement. is more effective political advertising for the 
Unabomber than anything we could dream up." 

Unapack also points out that it is winning the war of perceptions with the media 
on the character of the Unabomber. “When the manifesto was first published the 
media depicted him as a crazed psychopath with a mediocre intellect. Now he is 
universally recognized as a genius. The New York Times, which was hi-jacked by the 
Unabomber, labels him a genius on page one of this week's Sunday paper. This is a 


major concession. We are not aware of anyone who considers either Clinton or Dole a 


ge oo ae ae

Larry, I've never even voted before. How do I get to do a Unabomber write-in? 


Hey, it's easy, Rhonda! You've got to register thirty days before the election, or by October 5th, for the 
presidential final election on Tuesday, November 5th. Call the Election Commission in your town to find 
out how to register, and find out where you vote, and what the hours of the polling place are, and bring 
some ID. Ask the polling officials how to do a write-in vote on the balloting machine. Write-in Unabomber 
for president, not Kaczynski; he hasn't been proven to be the author of the manifesto, and besides, it's 
the ideas that matter, not the man. Be sure to lie to the exit pollers.

From Punk Magazine, 1977: 


RICHARD HELL: Basically, | have one feeling...the desire to get out of here. And any other feelings | 
have come from trying to analyze, you know, why | want to go away....See, | always feel 
uncomfortable and | just want to walk out of the room. It's not going to any other place or any other 
sensation, or anything like that, it's just to get out of "here." 


LEGS McNEIL: Where do you feel comfortable? 

RICHARD HELL: When I'm asleep. 

LEGS McNEIL: Are you glad you were born? 

RICHARD HELL: | have my doubts... Did you ever read Nietzche? 
LEGS McNEIL: Ha ha ha. 


RICHARD HELL: Legs, listen to me, he said that anything that makes you laugh, anything that's 
funny indicates an emotion that's died. Every time you laugh that's an emotion, a serious emotion 
that doesn't exist with you any more... and that's why I think you and everything else is so funny. 


LEGS McNEIL: Yeah, | do, but that's not funny. 
RICHARD HELL: That's cause you don’t have any emotions, ha ha ha. 


--Excerpted without permission from "Please Kill Me: An uncensored oral history of Punk" by Legs 
McNeil and Gillian McCain - anti-copyright 1996 


EE SSIIltr Ee 


SO YOU'RE A REPORTER? Or maybe an editor? A broadcaster? And you've found your way to the Unabomber 
'96 web page. 


What drew you here? Maybe you're reporting a story. Or maybe you thought this was pretty funny - Unabomber 
for president, ha ha ha. Read the Richard Hell quote above. It is used without permission from the galleys for a 
new book: "Please Kill Me: The uncensored oral history of Punk," by Legs McNeil and Gillian McCain (July 1996, 
elapse It was smuggled to us through Unapack's extensive network of media collaborators; the underground of 
the datasphere. 


YOU HAVE POWER? Really? As a member of the media, you do have one kind of power; that over other people's 
lives. You can make or break a person's reputation, their livelinood, their own grip on power. When you topple 
tyrants, it's a beautiful thing. When your profession abuses that power, the media itself becomes the tyrant. 


You have power over others, but do you have power over your own daily life? 
THERE WAS A TIME WHEN YOU WERE NOT A SLAVE. 


We, at Unapack, feel your pain. Racing from deadline to deadline. Processing information and packaging it to fit 
the "style" and vision of others. Expectations that you work overtime - you're a "professional" after all! Covering 
stories you have no passion for, or if you do have passion, having to narrow your focus to fit the requirements 
placed upon you by others. Are you satisfied? Have you expressed yourself? 


This is a letter we received in April 1996 from a very powerful television reporter in one of the top ten media 
markets: 


Chris and Lydia, 


Give me a call when you can (XXX-XXXX), or e-mail me here. I'd like to 
discuss a possible TV story on the Unapack page, but I'd like to talk with 
you first to get more information... goals, motives, etc. I found the page 
really interesting. Same with parts of paranoia.com. 


UNAPACK, P.0.B.120494, BOSTON, MA 02112 


E-MAIL: unapack@paranoia.com WEB:www.paranoia.com/unapack/ 


Reporter 
TV-X News 


To which Unabomber '96 campaign manager Lydia Eccles replied: 
XXXK - 


Did you speak with us at the Kerry Weld debate?? Please e-mail if you are 
still interested in the web page. By the way, this campaign is no joke. It 
is aimed at actually getting the votes. We feel that anyone who feels that 
the march of technology is inexorable and we must be in a reactive, 
adaptive mode has acknowledged that we are not free--that a system of 
political freedom cannot permit us to create the future we desire. Our 
campaign asserts that we ARE free to shape our future, that technology is 
not a natural force but an accident, and thus the first step is to leave 
"politics" behind and start dealing with the real factors that determine 
our lives. Thus, "are you ready for the rupture?" Are you ready for the 
rapture of utopian realism????? (Have I converted you yet?) Everything's 
possible. 


--Lydia 
To which the powerful TV reporter responded: 
Lydia, 
I didn't get to the debate. (I start work at 4AM). I have pitched the page 


as a story...but have been overruled by two different producers here. 
Please keep me posted on developments. I'm more than happy to try again as 


events develop. I believe it is a story... but I don't make the final 
call. 

Sincerely, 

XAXX ARXKXAXAK ‘ 

TV-X News 


Everybody believes this TV reporter is powerful; but he cannot even report on something he cares about. We, at 
Unapack, understand how bad this must make you feel. Wherever you go, the civilians treat you like somebody 

important. They want to be your friend, because you are the media. But the enlisted press sees you for what you 
are - for what they are - hey, sorry to break it to you, but have you ever considered the possibility that you might 
be... 


A WAGE SLAVE? 


We'd urge you to think about it, but we understand you probably don't have time to think. As a Consciousness 
Industry worker, you have a competitive job to do; beat the opposition, and capture the attention of the audience 
so you can rent it to advertisers. How do you get their attention? By scaring them, by arousing their desires within 
certain narrow confines of journalistic hegemony, or by becoming the filter between the audience and events that 
actually interest them. 


Do you ever feel that, in the competitive rush to deadline, you unconsciously - or intentionally - trample on the lives 
of people whether or not they deserve it? If the competing press is trying to toppie a political leader, you join the 
pile-on. If the news trucks are racing to another human tragedy, you enter the race. You say you have to, it's a 
competitive business. 


REMEMBER WHEN TECHNOLOGY WAS GOING TO LIBERATE YOU? Recent years have brought many new 
tools to your profession: fax machines, voice mail, the Internet, cable television. Was there not a time when you 
hoped these inventions would free you up to THINK about what you write or broadcast? But instead, have they not 
just made your job more hectic, and your work more alienating. 


More and more, in journalism as with all other professions, people are dealing directly with people less and less. 
We are dealing with representations of people; voices on the phone, research on Lexus, messages back and forth, 
office e-mail, teleconferencing, laptops, think of all the wondrous technologies you have adapted to! You are ready 
for the new economy! You have nothing to lose but your...

cannot be in office—an outright rejection of the current 
social system. In addition to Unabomber write-in votes,

UNABOMBER CAMPAIGN OPENS OFFICE IN NEW YORK CITY

Unapack will be bringing its "No More Progress As Usual" campaign to the Chicago 

Convention. According to Unapack's Lydia Eccles, "It's just good strategy to goto _— canvention 
Chicago. The boring, predictable and pompous ritual of the Democratic Convention 

provides an ideal backdrop for us, and we are counting on a post- ounce for the 

Unabomber write-in candidacy. Party conventions--the more controlled, the better--are a 


big plus for Unapack, because they breed apathy, and apathy is the first step toward 
casting a sabotage vote."

UNAPACK, 


Unapack opposes the mainstream media's offer of free TV time for "major' scouted. as 
a transparently self-serving racket. The free TV plan is a media effort to extend and 
formalize control over public debate. As part of the bargain, the media have gained FCC 
exemption from federal rules requiring equal access for all legally qualified candidates. 
By this "offer" the media gains the power to decide who will be heard and who will be 
silenced. 


Unapack is also announcing the opening of a Unabomber campaign office in New York 
City. Unapack New York's announcement stated, "We must have a discussion of real 
issues, we must have passion, we must have life in our political life!" The New York 
office is distributing flyers, bumper stickers, and campaign literature. 


Following the convention Unapack will continue its drive to formally register the 
Unabomber write-in campaign nationwide, so that each state will be legally obligated to 
count Unabomber votes separately, rather than burying voter alienation in the 
classification of "other". 


Other campaign activities include the ongoing distribution of.bumper stickers nationally 
and internationally via the Unapack web site, a free outdoor advertising campaign 
including billboards such as "Straighten up and Enjoy Life" and "Welcome to Boston, 
Home of Unapack", and a new outdoor poster advertising theme, "America is voting for 
the Unabomber." Unapack's web site was also featured on MSNBC's "The Site" on 
August 7.

CHRIS KORDA -- UNAPACK 1996 UNABOMBER PRESIDENTIAL WRITE-IN CAMPAIGN 
DEMOCRATIC NATIONAL CONVENTION 
CHICAGO, ILLINOIS 


THE PUBLISHING OF THE UNABOMBER’S MANIFESTO IN THE WASHINGTON POST WAS AN 
EXTRAORDINARY EVENT, AND ANY HONEST EXAMINATION OF THE SUBSEQUENT PRESS 
COVERAGE REVEALS A SIMPLE BUT IMPORTANT TRUTH: THE UNABOMBER HIT A NERVE. 
EVEN TIME MAGAZINE, SURELY A SYMBOL OF CORPORATE CONTROL, WAS SEEN QUOTING 
THE UNABOMBER AT LENGTH, AND SUPPORTING MANY OF HIS OBSERVATIONS. INDUSTRIAL 
SOCIETY HAS BEEN A DISASTER FOR THE HUMAN RACE, AND PEOPLE ARE HUMILIATED AND 
DEGRADED BY THE TECHNOLOGIES THEY’ VE CREATED. 


THE UNABOMBER PRESIDENTIAL WRITE-IN CAMPAIGN IS ABOUT REVEALING THE 
RESIGNATION THAT PEOPLE FEEL, THE DEEP CONVICTION THAT THEY ARE UTTERLY 
HELPLESS, THAT THEY HAVE NO CHOICE BUT TO JOIN THE PARADE, THAT THEIR FATES ARE 
DETERMINED BY FORCES FAR BEYOND THEIR CONTROL. ISN’T DILBERT REALLY JUST AN 
EXPRESSION OF RESIGNATION, OF PASSIVE AGGRESSION? HOW MANY PEOPLE SECRETLY 
HATE THEIR JOBS, AND SUBVERT THEIR BOSSES IN COUNTLESS SUBTLE WAYS? REVEAL THAT 
RESIGNATION, AND IT WILL TURN TO RESENTMENT AND RIGHTFUL ANGER. 


THE UNABOMBER PRESIDENTIAL WRITE-IN CAMPAIGN WANTS TO CHANNEL PEOPLE’S ANGER 
CONSTRUCTIVELY, BY DIRECTING IT AGAINST THE MOST OBVIOUS SYMBOL OF MASS SOCIETY 
AND CORPORATE CONTROL: THE MEDIA, WHOSE PRIMARY FUNCTION IS TO MAINTAIN 
NORMALCY AT ALL COSTS. NOTHING, NOT RAIN OR SNOW, NOT FLOODS OR DROUGHT, NOT 
TERRORIST BOMBINGS OR EVEN FULL-SCALE WAR CAN BE ALLOWED TO DISRUPT THE WELL- 
ORGANIZED HIVE OF WORKER BEES, DRIVING TO WORK, SLURPING DOWN THEIR COFFEE AND 
DONUTS, CLEAN, SMILING, HAPPY, WELL-DRESSED BEES, BUZZING IN CONFERENCE ROOMS 
AND CUBICLES, LINING UP IN SHOPPING MALLS TO SPEND THE MONEY THEY’ VE SACRIFICED 
SO MUCH FOR ON FASHIONABLE TRINKETS AND FOOD NEATLY WRAPPED IN PLASTIC. THE 
MEDIA RE THE BAND THAT KEEP THE TROOPS MARCHING FORWARD, NO MATTER HOW MANY 
COMRADES FALL, CROSSING OFF THE HALLMARK HOLIDAYS, ON CALENDAR AFTER 
CALENDAR, WITH A SPECTATOR SPORT FOR EVERY SEASON, REDUCING OUR FUTURE TO THE 
DRONING VOICE OF THE WEATHERMAN, ALWAYS THE SAME. 


THE UNABOMBER PRESIDENTIAL WRITE-IN CAMPAIGN IS A SERIOUS ELECTION EFFORT THAT 
AIMS TO TOTALLY UNDERMINE THE ELECTION PROCESS ITSELF, BY EXPOSING THE MEDIA’S 
EXCLUSION OF ALL MEANINGFUL DEBATE ABOUT THE NATURE AND DIRECTION OF OUR 
DAILY LIVES. THE USELESS CHARADE OF CHOOSING BETWEEN IDENTICAL WINGS OF THE 
PRO-BUSINESS PARTY, THE DEMICANS AND REPUBLICRATS, IS THE PALE GHOST OF 
DEMOCRACY IN A MASS SOCIETY SO VAST AND POWERFUL AND RUTHLESS THAT IT CAN 
ONLY BE CONTROLLED BY MACHINES. WHEN PEOPLE ARE ANGRY ENOUGH TO VOTE FOR THE 
UNABOMBER, THE MEDIA WILL HAVE NO CHOICE BUT TO DELIVER THE MESSAGE, EVEN IF IT 
MEANS DEATH FOR THE MESSENGER. VOTES FOR THE UNABOMBER CAN’T BE 
RATIONALIZED OR MEDIATED OR EXPLAINED AWAY. THEY ARE AN EXPRESSION OF RAGE, 
NOT APATHY, OF UTTER CONTEMPT FOR THE BRUTALITY AND INDIFFERENCE OF OUR 
SUPPOSEDLY “CIVILIZED” SOCIETY. 


FOUR HUNDRED YEARS AGO, OUR SUBURBS AND OFFICE PARKS WERE WILDERNESS, FOREST 
AND PLAINS, MOUNTAINS AND RIVERS, TEEMING WITH AN UNIMAGINABLE DIVERSITY OF 
LIFE. INDUSTRIAL SOCIETY CRUSHED OUT THAT DIVERSITY, AND REPLACED IT WITH 
MONOCULTURE: MILE AFTER MILE OF CORN FIELDS, EACH PLANT A GENETICALLY PERFECT 
COPY, IDENTICAL HOUSES AND CARS IN ENDLESS ROWS, ONE SIZE FITS ALL, EVEN PEOPLE 
STANDARDIZED AND STACKED ON TOP OF ONE ANOTHER LIKE CANS OF BEER. WHAT NATIVE 
SOCIETY EVER BUILT FACTORY FARMS, OR ROBOTIC SLAUGHTERHOUSES? WHAT MAKES US 
SO DIFFERENT FROM OUR VEAL COWS, FORCE-FED AND CHAINED TO THEIR PENS, UNABLE TO 
TAKE A SINGLE STEP? WHO WERE THE REAL SAVAGES? A VOTE FOR THE UNABOMBER IS A 
VOTE FOR THE CHAOS OF FREEDOM, A VOTE FOR WILD NATURE: DARE TO JOIN THE 
BARBARIANS AT THE GATES.

just got your snail-mail today wondering whether i'd like to be a 
'headquarters' for the campaign -- after some consideration and 
discussion with my friends and roommate, i want to say i would be 
more than happy, in fact, it would be an honor. 


my initial reaction was hesitation, due to the negative publicity 
it might draw -- considering the unabomber's status as 'terrorist' 
by media-engineered public opinion, campaigning for the unabomber | 
might be misconstrued by some as advocacy of terrorism. of course 
anybody who makes such a complaint would only assume so *because* 
they haven't read our platform . .. as one of the main points of 
the platform is to bring attention to the fact that bill clinton, 
bob dole and every other mainstream candidate, by virtue of their 

Bp lesspport for u.s. foreign policy (i.e. , military aggression, 

colonialization, imperialism) is *no less* a 'terrorist' than the 

unabomber. if you bring any of the candidat s under scrutiny, you — 


realize what we have here, is a very hazy definition of the term: 
'terrorist'. 


as i see it, the best campaign strategy we could possibly have is 


to present the reasons why the mainstream candidates -- clinton & 
dole, specifically & independant candidates to a lesser extent -- 
are just as despicable as we percieve the unabomber ... . given 


the evidence that is available for anybody who invests the time & 
effort to do a little research, this shouldn't be too difficult a 
task 


i recently finished reading the _manifesto_ -- and while i do not 
agree with every point (in particular, his reasoning that killing 
people is necessary to make a point) there is a *lot* of validity 
in his argument against technology. - . . . perhaps that is why i 
have been supporting your campaign in my zine from the beginning. 


so, once again, -- i accept your invitation, as do my friends. we 
plan to intitiate your campaign on our campus beginning with this 
weekend when we distribute your pamphlet at our coffeehouses. and 

just as soon as we receive the rest of the resources which you've 
available (press packages, flyers, stickers, etc.) we will see to 
it that the ‘unabomber campaign' is known throughout the state of 
north carolina. 


thank you, 
christopher

UNAPACK: THE UNABOMBER '96 PRESIDENTIAL WRITE-IN CAMPAIGN 
For immediate release: September 26, 1996 


UNABOMBER CAMPAIGN OPENS CHICAGO 
HEADQUARTERS 


UIC students running with the "pack" 


I am proud to announce the opening of a new Unabomber Presidential Write-In Campaign headquarters 
in Chicago. It is stationed on the campus of UIC, just west of the heart of the city. Many thousands of 
students on college campuses just like this pass through the classroom doors daily. I see it as just a bit too 
robotic and mechanical. A great number of the students find themselves here only because they don't 
want to be somewhere of lower profile. On this educational side of things, the Unabomber Campaign can 
help a lot of students realize that while they may not know which direction they are going, wandering 
through the classrooms just to keep from wandering the streets, they CAN express their true feelings. 


The major complaint pinned upon those supporting this campaign is that they are supporting violent acts 
against others to solve problems. However, this is far from the heart of the campaign, as it centers around 
the ideology, not actions, of the Unabomber. We are focused more on stressing the important themes 
brought up in his manifesto (which can be found on the Internet), than any political platform. Besides, this 
man is no more murderous than most other political figures, past or present, people just tend to view it 
the wrong way, the way they are compelled to view it, through the media's not-so-fair portrayal. 


Those supporting this outlook just want to speak out against the technologically advanced society we live 
in, and how it oppresses and lowers the profile of the working class, in addition to the environment. 
Educational standards just keep increasing, making it more than just a simple task to get a decent job. We 
have to go to school all of our younger years, the years we're supposed to enjoy, and work the rest. 
Before long, a Master's Degree will not be enough. Even then you won't be able to live on the streets 
because the air will be unbreathable. The Unabomber Campaign gives a place for the voices that would 
not normally be heard by just sitting out of the election and not voting. After all, this is a free country and 
we are entitled to a choice. 


Although the Unabomber will not serve if elected, the importance of the urgent industrial/technological 
situation, along with the drastic effects it has on the earth and its many inhabitants, will finally be a 
priority. These issues will no longer be easily moved down the list once it is evident that they are on top. I 
am not ashamed to support this campaign or the fire behind it, and will continue to spread the word 
among fellow students and other citizens wherever I travel throughout my life. This is about far more 
than any one election and will extend far beyond November 5. How can anyone point a finger our way 
when we are merely concerned about the present condition of this society and the environment future 
generations will have to live in? Are you running with us? 


-Justin, Unapack Chicago

Lydia Eccles on your presidential write-in choice for ‘96 


THE BOYS. Clinton, Gingrich, Powell, Perot, Forbes, Dole, Gramm, Lugar,Alexander, Dornan, Keyes, etc. 


HE'S HOT! His favorability ratings may be low, but his name recognition is close to 100%. We won't need to hype him--he's already hyped. A Unabomber write-in 

a campaign can surf the media wave. He's the perfect imposter to undermine the presidential election process as it unfolds, a ee omens 
itself,

CTED HE WILL NOT SERVE. It's a nobody-for-president vote. He's not running, so this can be a bottom-up free-for-all campaign. Campaign literature, 
sound bytes, platforms, pranks, the rest; have it your way, 


ON'T WASTE YOUR VOTE. The media's like a psychiatrist--and you can't NOT communicate in an election. If you boycott the polls, you'll be counted as apathetic, — 
complacent, or still worse, contented. If you vote for the mainstream lesser of evils, who don't actually represent your views, you've affirmed the political system and 
buried your voice. Either way you've wasted your vote. To vote for the Unabomber is to vote and boycott at the same time. If nothing else, it's a vote against the election 
charade. It can be only seen as absolute protest, ridicule, or a "none-of-the-above" spurning of the political menu. You can cast an anarchistic vote you feel good about, 
send the message that the presidential elections are a fraud. And you can still vote in local races and referendums where your vote counts for something. 


/OTE AGAINST THE PROPAGANDA MACHINE. The Unabomber did an end run around the media monopoly, and published without editorial clearance. The 
Inabomber has, by the magnitude of his plan, exposed the media as a closed communications system, making it very clear--in case anyone hadn't noticed--that it's a 
; nications war. Mass media are launched from a heavily-secured fortress. Other terrorists seek publicity as a means to other ends. The Unabomber used terrorism 

to gain publicity as an end in itself. Notice how the press seeks to channel interpretation of the Unabomber story, covering it as a serial-killer story of crime and insanity, 
excluding consideration of the ideas themselves. They would have us believe that it would be disastrous if media weren't controlled from the top. Op-ed pages 
with journalists lamenting, "Why didn't he have to get editorial approval? What if copy cats are aroused, crazies who actually want access to the media, rather 
i nply being passive target markets for political and commercial propaganda?" Imagine mass communications not subject to corporate control. People might say 
..even things not "fit to print". Exactly. When ABC Nightly News gets renamed Disney World, you'll cherish the memory of your Unabomber vote. 


T THE CREDENTIALS. The Unabomber's use of violence should not disqualify him from consideration. His willingness and ability to effectively use 
to achieve strategic political goals merely demonstrate the essential qualifications to be president. After all, Colin Powell's ONLY qualification is his 
rmance as an effective killer, No one's called him a serial killer, or said he craved attention. No running candidate has condemned the Gulf War genocide. This is a 
, SBeenay that ployee war like a video game in a high-tech funhouse. We aren't even allowed information as to how many Iraqis, civilian or military, our tax dollars blew 
; That Bill Clinton avoided the draft and hadn't killed was considered a lack of qualifications. Luckily he picked up points for presiding over numerous executions in 
home state of Arkansas. Occupational deaths and diseases... Violence? Cancer deaths caused by toxins in the air, in food, and workplaces...Violence? A minimum 

that is half the poverty level, with the hunger, stress, disease and early death that ensue... Violence? The media just finished re-elaborating the rationale for bombing 
hima and Nagasaki... Violence? Terror? Anyone bringing up violence should put it all on the table, not just select attacks on the power structure. Anyone who can 
take a stand against violence in any form—and that would include the American Revolution--can say the Unabomber shouldn't be president on that basis. But he's not 
anyway, and even a landslide wouldn't actually put him in office. That's the beauty of voting for a fugitive from the law. 


ERTAINMENT VALUE, Watch your favorite TV pundits try to swallow, digest and regurgitate a Unabomber constituency. It's a message that can't be neutralized 
‘ explained away. The most minimal Unabomber returns would disrupt the usual discussion of false problems and false solutions (usually known as "reform".) 

DON "T BLAME ME-I VOTED FOR THE UNABOMBER. You can sport your bumper sticker after the election... but not on a car! 

r who trespasses against the rules or ignores them is a "spoil sport". The spoil sport shatters the play-world itself. By withdrawing from the game, he reveals the 
d fragility of the play world. He robs play of its illusions.

METRO BEAT 


hink the election campaign 
is a bummer? How about 
the Unabomber for presi- 
dent? 

Even though President Clinton 
is an apparent shoo-in for re-elec- 
tion, he's hardly a favorite among 
voters, many of whom express such 
disaffection from both major parties 
they are either planning to stay 
home on election day or cast a 
protest vote for Ralph Nader or the 
Libertarian Party. 

A Boston group, Unapack, says 
it has a better idea, and has 
launched a Unabomber presiden- 
tial write-in campaign announcing 
that “mutant times call for mutant 
tools.” According to Unapack 
spokesperson Lydia Eccles, it’s a 
serious effort. 

“We’ve printed thousands of 
bumperstickers and brochures, and 
even have a billboard in downtown 
Boston promoting the campaign,” 
she says. A Brooklyn Unapack 
group hoisted a 60-foot write-in 
banner in the city’s Red Hook dis- 
trict. It was quickly removed by 
irate officials. 

Her group doesn’t idealize the 
Unabomber, says Eccles, but likes 
it that he “hijacked the New York 
Times and Washington Post for his 
(anti-technology) manifesto.” 

“The Unabomber is important 
because he’s the onty public figure 
raising the real issues about the de- 
struction of wild nature and the de- 
humanizing effect technology has 
on us,” adds Unapack’s Chris Ko- 
rda. 


Deeait MERO bl - 
Unabomber for president — 


crimes attributed to the Un- 
abomber, for which Ted Kaczynski 
has been charged in several states. 


- Eccles feels this twist on the presi- 


dential campaign’s so-called char- 
acter issue isn’t relevant to her can- 
didate. 

“Killing people has never mat- 
tered in this country as to whether 
a person is considered admirable 
or not,” she says, adding that most 


presidents bomb people in order to, 


rise in the polls. “Of all the candi- 
dates, the Unabomber is the only 
one who has vowed not to kill any 
more people.” 

Still, the campaign isn’t without 
whimsy. The New York City Una- 
pack affiliate faxed the media an 
announcement of the opening of 
their local Unabomber campaign 
office which listed a toll-free num- 
ber, 800-707-6398, at the bottom. 
However, when the number is di- 


- aled, instead of the Unapack cam- 


paign office, callers reach the tele- 
phone bank of the Republican 
Congressional Committee, which 
supports GOP House candidates. 

Ken Hill, a phone supervisor 
there, thinks listing the GOP num- 
ber on the Unabomber release is 
“some kind of counter-cultural 
thing.” As a result of it, Hill says 
the committee has received numer- 
ous calls from people complaining 
there’s no difference between his 
party and the Democrats. 

“Tt’s a thumb to the nose kind of 
thing— a practical joke,” he says. 
According to Hill, Republicans 
alerted their phone bank and will 


_ phony calls eine in. WE Spec

candidate needs at least three 


Finn. Say 


According to local cteeion offi- 
cials, Eccles’ and Korda’s group 
may have trouble getting their 
votes counted. Most states require 


write-in votes, so Unapack asks 
that “Unabomber/ Ted Kaczynski” 
be used, although they say this 
doesn’t imply an assumption of his 
guilt. 

In the Detroit area, votes for the 
unacandidate might not even be 
recorded since, according to South- 
field City Clerk Mary Bonner, a 


write-in votes to be tallied. 

“Plus,” she says, “you must be- 
long to an officially registered par- 
ty to be counted since, in a presi- 
dential election, strictly speaking, 
you vote for electors, not the candi- 
date.” 

Such impediments don’t dis- 
courage Unapack’s efforts. 

“Mainstream electoral politics 
are dealing with trivial issues while 
we are heading for disaster,” Eccles 
says. “There is massive denial of 
the environmental and social dam- 
age occurring.” 

Still, confidence in a victory isn’t 
running high at Unapack headquar- 
ters. They’ve already prepared a 
post-election campaign bumper- 
sticker which says, “Don’t Blame 
Me, I Voted For The Unabomber.” 
—Peter Werbe

Page 6 The TAB, October 29 - November 4, 1996 


News & Comment 


Unapack: Politics with 
°60s-style disruption 


Anarchist group backs Unabomber for 
president, aims to unravel modern life 


By Linda Rosencrance 
TAB Staff Writer 
y day they’re bookkeepers, artists, 
os computer technicians and programmers 
and carpenters. By night they’re 
Unapack — a Boston-based anarchist group 
staging a Unabomber for president write-in 
campaign. 

They meet in a Chinatown apartment dec- 
orated with Unabomber-for President-para- 
phernalia, as well as photographs and writ- 
ings that call to mind a time of turbulence in 
American history — the ’60s. 

Like their ’60s counterparts, members of 
Unapack — the Unabomber political action 
committee recognized nationally — question 
authority. And like the Unabomber they also 
question the role of technology in society — 
claiming that it has been a disaster for the 
human race. 

“The last time serious questioning went on 
was in the ’60s, which has now been buried, 
in part through co-optation,” said Lydia 
Eccles, manager for the Unabomber for 
President campaign. 

Eccles said Unapack endorses anything 
and everything — from not voting for pre- 
selected candidates to defaulting on credit 
cards to trespassing on corporate communi- 


‘Setoins beset isthe ies fotos tiate 


cations (i.e., putting up illegal billboards) — 
that will keep society from functioning nor- 
mally. 

In fact, one of Unapack’s slogans is “Just 
undo it.” 

In 1968 at the Democratic National 
Conventional in Chicago, anti- Vietnam War 
protesters garnered media attention by nomi- 
nating a pig for president in order to make a 
statement about political corruption, abuse of 
police power and the irrelevance of national 
elections. 

This year, Eccles and Chris Korda, another 
Unapack organizer, faked press credentials 


and infiltrated the Democratic National 
Convention, coincidentally also in Chicago, 
which allowed them to promote their presi- 
dential candidate, the Unabomber. 

According to Eccles, Unapack began 
pitching the idea of the Unabomber for presi- 
dent last April, shortly after publication of 
the bomber’s manifesto. 

However, Eccles said, Unapack is not pro- 
moting alleged Unabomber, Ted Kaczynski as 
president, though the group does endorse the 
35,000-word manifesto he allegedly wrote. 

Kaczynski, currently being held in a 
California jail, is charged with seven of the 
16 bombings. In the bombings that include 
those for which he is charged, three died and 
23 people were injured. 

“Although the Unabomber will not serve 
if elected, he represents a complete reversal 
in perspective from the consensus of the 
main candidates who run,” Eccles said while 
being interviewed about the campaign on a 
national radio station. “He symbolizes attack- 
ing the monologue, the monopoly of the 
press as well as the anti-industrial concept of 
society.” 

Eccles said Unapack has been successful 
in getting its message out to all parts of the 
country through mailings, illegal billboards, 
bumper stickers and a presence on the 
Internet — www.paranoia.com/unapack/ 

Until Nov. 5, Unapack will be working 
hard trying to get people to cast write-in 
votes for the Unabomber. 

“Tf enough concemed citizens actually cast 
this write-in vote, we will rupture the 
pompous election ritual into a utopian 
moment and take our stand against technoc- 
racy before it destroys us entirely,” Eccles 
said. “If everyone who normally stays home 
because of resignation and votes we will 
win.” O

We wish to publicly announce the opening of a 

UNABOMBER FOR PRESIDENT office here in New York 

City, and the beginning of our grassroots campaign to convince 
registered voters to write the name Unabomber in on their 
ballots in the presidential election to be held November 5, 1996. 

? We firmly believe that voting Unabomber is the only 

Alfgrnative in a “coftest” that excites, impassions or energizes 
exactly no one, neither the supporters nor the opponems of 
Democratic incumbent Shill Clinton, Republican candidate 
Asshole Dole or Reform Party candidate Dross Perot. 

We are confident that others will immediately grasp the 
humor, irony and appropriateness of casting an absurd protest 
vote ~ in a “grid-locked” élection -- for a decidedly non- 
commercial and yet widely-published sare a long and sober 
theoretical text about industrial society, who FS also being held 

without bail on charges of sending explosive devices through =< 
the mail.

‘ considerations should not dissuade ws. 

We must have discussion of real isswes, we must have 

passion, we must have life in our political life!
