Subject: Re: waking up and finding out that -- 
To: William.J.Brown@bender.com (William J. Brown) 
Date: Wed, 6 Nov 1996 13:54:10 -0600 (CST) 


Hi Billy- 


We had a greatday! I forget if I e-mailed you about it yet, but’ the 
night before theelection we got the new political signs at major polling 
booths in Cambridge, Jamaiaca Plain, Brookline,Roxbury, and Boston. It 
really looked great because our signs definitely the most attractive, 
and we had as many as the others did. Also got 100 wheatpasted flyers 
using the Gary photos. Converged on Boston's biggest polling place with 
many signholders, stole all the attention from the others, and were the 
first group interviewed on Boston's biggest talk radio station--We told 
her that Perot had stolen the Unabomber's year-old campaign slogan "don't 
wste your vote", how big we are, a few other things, then she said, "Why 
not just vote for Ralph Nader? " and i said, well, as the manifesto 
says, revolution is easier than reform" and she looked really pissed, 
because it was going out live (including being broadcast from a mobile 


truck at the polling place) and walked off. Actually, I don't a. | 


line llike to use the word revolution, but I like that phrase alot, it's kind 
of a good sound bite. All the pollworkers for the 

other candidates wanted bumperstickers, and wanted to have or trade for 

our signs. Some of them are going to come to the victory party--On the 

subway on the way home a guy wanted to trade us a clinton/gore sign for a 
unabomber sign. 


Also, I just got Fifth estate from Detroit. I won't say anymore--just 


Check it out ! It should be at black and red, right? 

Got excellent reactions to the Gary flyers (series of five, including the 
guy 

from New York. People want them. A few people told me it made their 
day. 


Got some good shots of our big signs on the boarded up windows of a 
MacDonald's nearby that had afire recently. They were up all day, right 
by a street light on an extremely busy traffic route (including 
pedestrian traffic) and just standing around I heard everyone talking 
about them as they went by. Had a bunch on a construction wall on 
Boylstong Street too, theat remained up. 


Chris wrote a letter to the Phoenix concerning and article they wrote about “ 
the guy who ripped off my 

Nixon poster and the unabomber stickers for his commercial T-shirt ventur 
...He lies in the article and claims to have had permission for the Nixon 
thing, and further saying that I had approached him and given him the 
Unabomber design!!! Anyway, they said they'd print a letter (tocorrect) 
and Chris talks about Unapack in the letter. Peter Werbe sent me the 
Detroit Metro article. 


Anyway, yesterday was really good--Icouldn't believe how many people : 
wanted stuff, wanted to talk about it, and it was wonderful when people 
came up and knew about the campaign and were really excited to see us 
out, and meet us. Some hung out and held signs for a while, too. At 
five o'clock Jamie roared up in his pickup truck with a big unabomber 
sign taped to the back and the radio blasting, and started unloading 
signs, and all these "volunteers" were showing up, and we were having 
such a great time and I think the other pollworkers felt kind of jealous 
of our panache. 


Of course there were the usual freaks--This overdressed Back Bay Brahmin 
came up to me and hissed, (as if I were a child) "You should be ASHAMED of 
yourself!" I said, "I'm not ashamed of myself at all, and in fact I 

think YOU should be ashamed of yourself if you're voting for Clinton, 

Dole or Perot!" "He killed people" "Who are you voting for who didn't 

kill people?" "Well, at least he didn't know who the people were who he 
BAR A Ved!" (22?) Lots of people wanted flyers and info. It ws alsofun 
greeting the voters --The Kerry person would say, Hi I hopeyou'11 \fote 

for Kerry for Senator and we'd add "And the Unabomber for president..." 


Oh well, got to take a nap. Igot a big letter from Al yesterday about how 

great the campaign was and wanting to reconcile again. Also filled with 

a huge paragraph of thgings he had heard from "friends" about my negative 
attitude toward him. "Friends" is a woman named Jackie, who you may have 

met since she's bonded with Al and has been visiting him down in New York 

alot. I was so incensed by what she had said to him that I responded to 

his letter--but now I hve to figure out how to deal with his desire for 
freindship. The letter also included lots of political hyperbole and 

quotes from a spanish anarchiist that he's currently reading. I don't i 
want to be nasty to him, but I also know that I simply cannot relate to his 


form of political consciousness, the grand gesture, the invocation of 
celebrity leaders, the idolizing of rock stars and other mainstream 
communicators/marketers, the mythologizing and self-mythologizing, the 
rhetoric, etc. 

It's exactly that that I think should be avoided! So I really don't 
want to have any unapack projects appropriated, even with good 
intentions, to serve antithetical goals. The whole thinkg is tremendously 
awkward. 


yh Yew gor Not Bored! yesterday, and that was a treat! I'm hoping to get a 
chance to read it in full today. 


I don't think I should have a dinner the night before the thing, because 
I'll probably (definitely) have to be working on preparations. 
Will you still be hear on the 16th? Are you going back on Sunday night? 


Are you 
inviting Al? Do whatever you think is appropriate. 

Lydia

December 13, 1996 
Dear Director of Elections: 


We are writing to you to request information about the results of the 1996 presidential 
election in your state. Unapack conducted a national write-in campaign for the 
Unabomber throughout the election year, and thus we would like to obtain information 
concerning how many write-in votes were cast for either “the Unabomber" or "Ted 
Kaczynski". 


This is not a frivolous request. The campaign had eight campaign headquarters across 
the nation, aroused national press interest, and distributed campaign literature, posters 
and bumperstickers nationwide. 


We hereby request all and any information you can provide to us concerning the 
tallying, count or results of presidential write-in votes in your state. What were the total 
write-in votes for president in your state? !f the write-in votes were broken out, how 
many did our campaign receive? If they were partially broken out (for certain 
candidates) what were those results? (What candidates' votes were counted and how 
many votes did they receive respectively?) If they were not broken out, is there any 
way for us to obtain this information? What is your complete policy on the counting of 
write-in votes? Does your state count as write-in votes votes for “non-persons” (cartoon 
characters, fictional personalities, etc.)? If you cannot provide us with the 
Unabomber/Kaczynski write-in vote count information we are requesting, please state 
in detail why you cannot. 


The information and responses we receive from state election officials will be made 
available to the press and posted on our campaign webpage to inform Unapack 
volunteers and supporiers. We appreciate your assistance and would appreciate 
hearing from you as soon as possible. 


Thank you. 


Lydia Eccles 


Unapack 


"We have grasped the situation, and we know what ought to be done."

Unapack letter to Director of Elections requesting write-in vote data

Response from Lisa K Daniel, State Election Director, Arizona 


JANE DEE HULL 
SECRETARY OF STATE 
STATE OF ARIZONA 


December 30, 1996 


Lydia Eccles 
Unabomber 96 
P.O. Box 120494 
Boston, MA 02112 


Dear Ms. Eccles: 


| respond to your letter dated December 13, 1996, in which you request 
information about the number of write-in votes that Arizona voters cast for the 
Unabomber. 


As Arizona’s election director and as a taxpayer, | am disgusted at your 
attempt to make a mockery of the election process by including an accused 
murderer as a write-in candidate for President. Since Mr. Kaczynski has been 
portrayed in the media as a recluse and he undoubtedly is busy preparing for his 
trials, it seems unlikely to me that he is a participant in your desire to “subvert the 
election” — a phrase you will recognize because it came from your website. 


While technology is changing the way ballots are counted in this country, 
write-in votes must be tallied by hand. When people like you undertake 
campaigns to encourage voters to write in the name of a joke candidate, you not 
only deprive your followers of casting a meaningful ballot, but you also cost the 
taxpayers of this country untold dollars in the hand processing of the ballots that 
contain write-in votes. Taxpayer’s money should not be wasted just for your 
amusement. 


Arizona tallies only the write-in votes cast for write-in candidates who 
submit the required paperwork by the fourteenth day prior to the election. Since 
Mr. Kaczynski did not submit papers to be listed as a write-in candidate for 
President, any votes cast for him were not recorded. 


Please make sure that you include my letter on your webpage. saad / ! 
Sincerely, 
isa K. Daniel 


State Election Director 


1700 WEST WASHINGTON, 7TH FLOOR PHOENIX, ARIZONA 85007-2888 | PHONE (602) 542-4285 FAX (602) 542-1575

Above & Opposite: 

1 October 1996 

Unapack, Don’t blame me! (bumper sticker) 

NB: As promised in Top Ten Reasons to Vote Unabomber—the final post-election campaign sticker 


“While | was at printing the ‘Don’t Blame Me’ stickers, | made a couple more post-election stickers. 
The tagline got smeared: “In the year 2000 there will be no election”. In fact, the 2000 election was 
disputed and remained unresolved for months.“—Lydia Eccles 


Hello: 


My name is Stacey Woelfel and I am conducting research at the University of 
Missouri focusing on the use of the Internet in the race for United States 
president this year. You have been identified as the operator of a 
political web site. It would be greatly appreciated if you would take a 
moment to reply to this e-mail and answer the questions below about your 
web 

site. This survey has been sent to every person operating a political web 
site dealing with this presidential election. The information requested is 
for academic use only and will not be released in any way until after the 
election. Thank you. 


VVVVVV VV VV VV V VV 


1. Which, if any, candidate does your web site support? If your web site 
> does not represent a candidate, what group or organization does it 

line 1> represent? 

The website is for Unapack, which campaigned for the Unabomber as a 
presidential write-in vote.> > 

> 2. Is your web site "officially" run by an organization or a candidate's 
> campaign, or is it an "unofficial" site run by a political supporter or 

> enthusiast? 

It is an "official" site, operated by Unapack, since the Unabomber is in 
jail, and of course did not initiate the campaign. > 


3. Have any of the candidates actually visited the site on-line? 
No, again, not possible 


4. On what date did the site go on-line? 
March 1, 1996. 


Where is the main web server physically located (city and state)? 
1 in California. 


6. How many people per week visit the site on-line? 

Depended on when. When Ted Kaczynski was arrested we were getting 
3,000 for a few days. It slowed down when he was out of the headlines. 
As the campaign grew, the campaign itself --rather than people doind 
searches on the interenet --attrated people dues to press,distribution of 
line 24literature, etc., by the end of the campaign we were getting his 
1200-1400/week.> > 
7. In your own words, what is the "mission" of the web site? > > 
To serve as an introduction to the campaign, to advocate the write-in 
vote, to be an instant press kit, and in a larger sense, to disrupt the 
political system, and since we were disseminating "dangerous ideas" that 
most press were reluctant to communicate without ttempting to discredit 
at the same time, it was also a way to provide unmediated access to our 
ideas. We also funded the campaign by selling bumper stickers, which 
were promoted on the page. 
> 8. List the top three characteristics that make this site worth a visit by 
> on-line users. 

1. Most interesting graphics, photos (images were "lifted" and used by 
almost all press who covered the campaign, including the NY Times, Time 
Magazine, Washington Post, Sand Francisco Tribune, etc. 

2. Best ideas and writing (page has been called brilliant, provocative, 
interesting, many people e-mailed with a desire to have e-mail 
discussions of ideas presented.) 

3. Press page, in which much of press was reproduced, so that readers 
could compare ideas in page with press coverage of it, thus see the 
process by which most press attempted to channel interpretation of the 
campaign. It showed that the page itself was subversive of the media, 
including the document "secret instructions to the media". 
Line sS—8—- How 
many people regularly maintain 

the site? 
Two. 

> > > 10. What is the monthly cost of maintaining the site? 
About $8, not including off web reprographics.> 

> 


> 11. Does funding for the site come from campaign funds or from some other 
> source? If some other source, what is that source? 
> Campaign funds. 
>

7 November 1996 

Unapack email communication 

NB: Election Research conducted by Stacey Woelfel, University of Missouri 


“The Unabomber Campaign owes a debt of gratitude to its many 
volunteers. To name a few, essential collaborator Reverend Chris Korda, 
who brought glamour, eloquence, press ferocity and webcoding skills while 
juggling Church responsibilities; political analyst “america” (preferring 
anonymity) who was available for consultations 24-7; Jamie Wheelock who 
helped with everything including street posting and attending the debates; 
Xander, Boston volunteers who campaigned in New Hampshire; CrimethInc. 
Ex-Workers Collective and the band Catharsis that printed the manifesto as 
a pamphlet and distributed it on music tours with Unapack materials and 
published materials in their zines; Al Giordano, political journalist at the 
Boston Phoenix (until he quit the newspaper and the campign in a rage and 
fled to New York); Bill Brown, Unapack New York; attorney Bob Black, 
Unapack Albany (author of The Abolition of Work, member of the Church 
of the Subgenius); Chris Blosser, Unapack North Carolina; Justin, Unapack 
Chicago, Anti-Authoritarians; anarcho-primitivist philosopher John Zerzan; 
Jesse from Eugene; zines who republished “Ten Reasons to Vote Unabomber’ 
and the ‘Dare to Be Perky! sticker distribution flyer, The Church of 
Euthanasia’s Snuff It, The Noise, Abrupt, TimeBomb, Weapon (because the 
truth hurts), The Open Eye, Loompanics, Inside Front, Harbinger. and many 
people who corresponded frequently.” 


—Lydia Eccles 


FEDERAL PUBLIC DEFENDER 
EASTERN DISTRICT OF CALIFORNIA 
801 K STREET, 10TH FLOOR 
SACRAMENTO, CALIFORNIA 95814 


Since you have shown an interest in Ted Kaczynski’s case, we are sending you the 
following information. 


On May 15, 1997, United States Attorney Paul L. Seave filed notice of intent to seek the 
death penalty against Ted Kaczynski. The decision to seek the death penalty was apparently 
made by United States Attorney General Janet Reno. 


On March 3, 1997, Ted Kaczynski’s. attorneys filed a motion to suppress the evidence 
seized by the FBI from his cabin, on the grounds that the FBI intentionally or recklessly misled 
the judge who issued the search warrant. On June 27, 1997 United States District Judge Garland 
E. Burrell denied this motion. 


On July 11, 1997, Ted Kaczynski’s attorneys filed a supplemental motion to suppress 
evidence on different grounds. At this writing, Judge Burrell has issued no decision on the 
supplemental motion. 


Copies of the relevant legal documents are available if you want them. 


Thank you for your interest in Ted Kaczynski’s case. 


Above: 
July 1997 
Note sent with an FBI photocopy of the Maniffesto 


Opposite: 

May 1997 

Lydia Eccles, Portrait of anarcho-primitivist philosopher John Zerzan in Eugene, Oregon 
NB: John Zerzan’s best-known books are Future Primitve and Elements of Refusal 


“Eugene is a hotbed of anarchism. During the Unabomber campaign, Anti-Authoritarians Anonymous and John 
Zerzan had distributed Unapack materials to his extensive West Coast network. In May 1997, as Ted Kaczynski 
awaited his trial to be held in November, John and | met to collaborate in organizing trial support for Ted through 
Unapack, since it had already gathered a constituency. Crimethinc. Ex-Workers Collective joined us and distributed 
their own edition of the Manifesto and Unapack materials as they toured the country with their metal punk band, 
Catharsis. 


The website was frozen on May 5, 1997 when Ted was sentenced, and The Manifesto Project distributed pre-trial 
support posters and stickers and gathered expressions in a participatory and growing zine to be re-circulated to its 
contributors. The posters and stickers by neccessity were independant of Ted Kaczynski and did not assume guilt. 


By June, John was visiting Ted in prison and communicating with his lawyers while the defense strategy was a 
mystery. Over the summer, as the judge denied all efforts by Ted’s lawyers to exclude evidence seized from his 
cabin—including his diary—a guilty verdict became a virtual certainty. We sent a Manifesto Project package to 
Ted through his lawyers. Scharlette Holdman, defense team death penalty mitigation specialist, told John that they 
absolutely loved it.”—Lydia Eccles

THE

INDUSTRIAL SOCIETY 
AND ITs FUTURE 


PREFACE 


THE UNABOMBER: A HERO For Our TIME — 


Pop quiz: What is it called when one of the finest minds of a 
generation picks a few individuals who are personally involved in the 
destruction of the environment (a timber-industry lobbyist) or of the 
attention span and reasoning ability of thousands of Americans (an 
advertising executive), and kills or maims them in the pursuit of 
finding a voice for his concerns about social issues... concerns that. 
otherwise would be heard by very few? 

Clearly, it is murder. 

And what is it called when a nation of overweight barbers and overpaid 
clerks, of lazy unemployed middle class intellectuals and talk-show-educated 
housewives, of cowardly fast-food-chain managers and racist sorority girls, 
conspire together to execute this murderer in the name of protecting the 
glorious status quo from his obviously deranged “mad bombings”? 

The death penalty. And rightly applied, too, in defense of the right of 
forest clear-cutters and professional liars to continue bending our world to 
their beautiful vision without the danger of being molested by those who 
prefer redwood forests to Quik-Marts and sonnets to detergent slogans. 

Seriously, and rhetoric aside, what is the difference between the two 
situations? In the one case, a single person evaluates his situations, and - 
decides upon a course of action that he feels is right. In the other case, 
millions of people, who are not very used to really making up their minds by 
themselves, feel strongly all together to choose to strike out rather blindly 
against an individual who does not remain within their boundries of accept- 
able behavior. 

Now, our gentle and moderate reader would no doubt like to object that 
it is not fear of the free-standing individual that prompts the outcry against 
this terrorist, but rather moral indignation—for he has taken ‘innocent’ life in 
his quest to. have his ideas heard, and that is wrong in every situation. 

But-this nation of petty imbeciles is not regularly outraged about the 
taking: of i innocent life: as long. as it fits within the parameters of the existing 
status. quo, they don’t care at all: 

How many more.people than the Unabomber have tobacco companies 
maimed and killed, by using advertising to addict them at a very young and 
uninformed age to an extremely harmful drug? How about the companies 
that advertize and sell cheap liquor in neighborhoods filled with alcoholics? 
How many citizens of third world nations have suffered and died at the 
hands of governments supported by such corporations as Pepsi Co., or even 
by the U.S. government itself? .And how much animal life is destroyed 
thoughtlessly every year, every day in death-camp factory farms... or in 
ecological destruction brought about by such companies as Exxon (our 
reader will remember the Valdez) or McDonalds (one of the better known 
destroyers of the rainforest)? No one is particularly concerned about these 
abuses of innocent life.

August 24, 1997 


Theodore Kaczynski 

c/o Scharlette Holdman 
529 Castro Street 

San Francisco, CA 94114 


Dear Ted: 


| wanted to write to let you know that | am going to cease organizing efforts around the 
trial unless called upon by you or Scharlette. Unfortunately | just sent a huge batch of 
stuff to you, which I'm sure is unwelcome, and I'm sorry about that. | hope that | have 
not been harmful to you. Just so you know, | have never represented to anyone that 
our organizing efforts are approved of or connected to you in any way. _| think I've 
told you that last year's year's "campaign" originated from the manifesto and the 
fugitive "FC" in September of 95, and was always kept separate from you. 


It has been difficult to know how or whether to proceed, and and | guess | made the 
wrong decision. But! was equally afraid that sitting still would be a wrong decision too. 
| will understand more as events unfold, and | hope that you manage to control the trial 
according to your goals. | donot, and may never know whether or how you are 
related to the work I've been doing, and that uncertainty and non-connection has 
been part of the paradox of doing it. | realize that | am only one element in the public 
response that you have had to deal with and that | have been operating in the dark. 
Actually, | feel pretty bad about my judgment at this point. 


| hope you also realize that my long-term concern with the ideas raised by these events 
is my sincere motivation. | will continue working on this in other ways, and | think | will 
do better work for having gone through these past two years. | will probably continue 
to use an ‘arty' goofy approach because it's a conscious, rational tactic which | 
believe generates some unique possibilities. 


| may pop you general interest things now and then, because | still assume it's nice to 
get mail, but just as a member of the well-wishing public from now on--not the kind of 
personally demanding letters I've sent you in the past. | wish you all the strength and 
firmness symbolized by my little heaven symbol on the posters. 


Sincerely and with good wishes, 


Lydia 


24 August 1997 

Lydia Eccles letter to Ted Kaczynski 

NB: On August 24, the defense team communicated through John Zerzan that 
Unapack should stop organizing support, providing no explanation

Dear Ms. Eccles: 


We have received your latest letter to Mr. Kaczynski 
regarding your organizing and publicity efforts. We 
appreciate the fact that you are being so cooperative in 
this respect. There is no need for you to worry about 
your past publicity efforts; no harm has been done. 


Mr. Kaczynski appreciates your messages of support. 
Perhaps Mr. Kaczynski will be able to correspond with 
you directly at some time in the future. 


Sincerely,

Above: 
18 September 1997 
Letter to Lydia Eccles from Quin Denvir (one of Ted Kaczynski’s lawyers) 


Following: 
November 1997 
Lydia’s journal entry & Unapack website images 


11/9/97 


Decided last night to go ahead with political support for Ted. This followed from having 
Green Anarchist list Unapack as the support Ted address; an article in the British 
Telegraph completely about Unapack; And a talk radio guy contacting me to do a 
two hour show in Salt Lake City. 


All of this made me feel a sense of the press about to swoop down upon the trial, and 
knowing that they will check the Unapack page, and so will others who would like to 
commune with Pro-Ted people. | do not think it's right to have this go down with out 
passionate political support for Ted. 


| decided that the original intent of the manifesto was to activate people like us. It has 
been very ambiguous this lengthy wait. We kept thinking we would at some point know 
what the strategy was, and thus how to react. But with Ted ndi cooperating with the 
examiners, and with my impression that he has not be really cooperating with his 
lawyers advice all along -- otherwise why would they wait until August to call us off? All 
of this indicates to me that Ted would like his ideas to be aired as much as possible. But 
from reading the biography, | also feel that he is probably in anguish at being in the 
spotlight and the object of acrimony, not to mention being thrown together with his 
family. But further, | don't think that political support for the Unabomber can hurt Ted 
since it is not connected to him. And even further, my original reason for getting 
involved was my feeling of the importance of the anti-tech ideas, not loyalty to a 
particular person. | think that if | can accept Ted killing people to bust things open, 
then | can't then say that cause isn't as important as the off chance that Ted would do 
better without political support. | feel it is historically important that there be visible 
support for Ted. Without it there will be extreme demoralization of all radical anti-tech 
people, who will feel isolated and unconnected. This, afterall, is how it makes me feel.

Dear Ted: 


John tells me that the trial begins on November 12, and that he will be there. | ama 
bookkeeper, so | am very tied up with year end things for my “clients” (!) (they have to 
spend all their money before the year end, float checks, then rush money back into 
their bank accounts in time to make the first payroll in January), there fore | am hoping 
to come at some point after Christmas. | really am not interested in seeing the 
prosecution at work anyway. Of course, after writing to you about the insanity defense 
| then read that you were not cooperating with prosecution mental examiners, so 
obviously | don't really know what the heck is going on! Sorry to be presumptuous as 
usual. 

| hope that you are not having to be medicated to support your legal defense. 
| feel that one of the most important points (and ignored points) made in the manifesto 
is the manipulation of human identity through drugs and ultimately genetic “therapies”, 
which to me are just a logical extension of the internalization of coercive authority (from 
police to progaganda to physicians). | am studying this right now as it unfolds in

grants to the state to fund state public service announcements advocating drug 
therapy for depression. Elli Lilly is very actively engages in crossing the line to genetic 
manipulations, and is partners with Monsanto, global “pioneer” in agriculture genetic 
engineering and admininstration of drugs to farm animals, bovine growth hormone, etc. 
“We are the veal" indeed! Anyway, it occurred to me that perhaps your strategy might 
entail being prescribed anti-schizophrenic drugs, and | know that that could be very 
discouraging, since of course it makes it impossible to think clearly, concentrate, 
remember, etc. Hope not! But even if so, surely it would be temporary. 

| continue to receive communication from people who are concerned about 
your situation and who wish to express solidarity with you. | wouldn't want to overstate 
the numbers - most people do just accept the media point of view without much 
skepticism — but those who see through it really see through it, and care very deeply. 

Well, | just wanted to write you a note before you have to step into the limelight 
of the trial to say stay strong, fuck the media, and very best wishes to you and 
Scharlette. | hope you're not overwhelmed with dread. Thinking back to the time of 
your arrest, you have the capacity to radiate dignity and strength under any 
circumstances. As to personal stuff, however bad it gets, at least you're not Bill Clinton! 
Well, | don't know what else fo say, just want you to know that as the trial proceeds | will 
be thinking about you. | will try to send you interesting things, but | don't really know 
what would hit home at this point. Maybe later | can get my friend Taylor Stoehr to dig 
up some unpublished Paul Goodman material for you. Or maybe some copies from a 
catelogue of German visonary artist Joseph Beuys. If | meet Scharlette I'll ask her if 
you'd prefer literature, or maybe John can ask her what kind of things you enjoy 
getting. Or | could just tell you incredible and smutty gossip about my insane friends!

targets.

from 23 Northern California coun-

district, from the Central Valley to 
the Oregon border. About 600 po- 
tential Kaczynski jurors gathered 
last month at the state fairgrounds 
to fill out questionnaires asking ba-

and whether a long trial would be a 
hardship.

scheduled to begin Wednesday 
with 12 jurors a day being ques- 
tioned further by U.S. District 
Court Judge Garland Burrell Jr. 
It’s common in federal court for 
judges to do most of the initial 
juror questioning.

INAS Erde EN 


Man Behind the Mask 


The accused Unabomber's lawyers say he's 
schizophrenic, but can they use that as a defense? 


By DAVID S. JACKSON SACRAMENTO 


HEN HE ENTERS THE COURT- 

room, all conversation — stops. 

Everyone stares as the man ac- 

cused of conducting an 18-year 
campaign of terror as the Unabomber 
walks to his seat. Even the prosecutors 
stop shuffling their papers to sneak a 
glance. But anyone expecting the self- 
confident strut of a killer who once 
branded his victims “dumb” and the 
FBI “a joke” will be disappointed. Ted 
Kaczynski’s courtroom demeanor is al- 
most timid. From the way he sits in his 
chair, hands folded, to the deferential be- 
havior he shows his attorneys, he moves 
with the exaggerated politeness of a guest 
who doesn’t quite know how to act in 
someone else’s home. 

Behind that placid exterior, however, 
is a stubborn defiance that could spell 
disaster for his defense. This week, as jury 
selection got under way in Sacramento, 
Calif., for his trial on federal charges of 
killing two men and _ seriously 
wounding two others with package 
bombs, Kaczynski’s defense strategy 
is in turmoil. The first public sign of 
trouble was the Harvard graduate’s 
abrupt refusal to be examined by 
prosecution psychiatrists. But TIME 
has learned that he initially resisted 
examination by even his own doc- 
tors. This stance might be endorsed 
by the “Unabomber Manifesto,” 
which denounces anyone who at- 
tempts to “control human behay- 
ior,” but it could seriously jeopardize his 
attorneys efforts to save his life. They had 
planned to argue that Kaczynski suffers 
from paranoid schizophrenia, which 
made him incapable of the intent neces- 
sary for him to be held legally responsible 
for the crimes. But now U.S. District 
Court Judge Garland Burrell Jr. is weigh- 
ing a prosecution request to bar all expert 
psychiatric testimony, leaving his defense 
in tatters. 

Historically, defendants who claim in- 
sanity or mental disease in federal trials 
rarely succeed, But if the jury in this case is 
allowed to hear details about paranoid 
schizophrenia, they may see some disturb- 
ing parallels with Kaczynski’s life. For ex- 
ample, psychiatrists say true schizophren- 


GAMMA LIAISON; ELAINE THOMPSON—AP (INSET) 


ics often resist diagnosis. “They don’t like to 
think of themselves as mentally ill,” says 
Dr. Ira Glick, a professor of psychiatry at 
Stanford. “They'd think something else 
caused their problems, like bad parenting 
or bad government or too many drugs— 
anything but being labeled crazy.” Kaczyn- 
ski has lashed out at both his parents 
and government. 

The mystery illness that sent Kaczyn- 
ski to the hospital when he was only 10 
months old could take on new significance. 


Some researchers believe that schizo- 
phrenia could come from a virus that 
strikes pregnant mothers and infants, caus- 
ing brain damage that usually doesn’t be- 
come fully apparent until the teens or ear- 
ly 20s. Kaczynski’s family has said he was 
always an antisocial child and that his be- 
havior got worse as he got older. At 26, he 
abruptly resigned from a prestigious teach- 
ing post at the University of California, 
Berkeley, and dropped out of society. The 
first Unabom attack occurred three days af- 
ter his 36th birthday. 

Schizophrenia is an irreversible dis- 
ease whose symptoms can be curbed but 
not cured by drugs, according to experts. 
Is it possible for someone to suffer from 
paranoid schizophrenia and function for 


18 years? Says Glick: “If you pull yourself 
out of society, live alone and are not mar- 
ried or dating, you can go a long time.” 
From their first contact with the FBI, 
the family warned that Kaczynski had 
severe mental problems. And _ three 
months after his arrest on April 3, 1996, at 
his mountainside cabin outside Lincoln, 
Mont., family attorney Anthony Bisceglie 
cited Kaczynski’s mental illness as a reason 
the government should not seek the death 
penalty. “In his correspondence, Ted pro- 
jects his own feelings of anger, depression 
and powerlessness onto society at large— 
a society of which he has never really been 
a member,” Bisceglie wrote lead pros- 
ecutor Robert Cleary. “He blames these 
ill effects on a wide variety of external 
factors, including childhood classmates, 
teachers and his family as well as the 
media, chemical and electronic mind 


KACZYNSKI, lower right, with fellow Merit scholars in his high school 
yearbook, was bright but antisocial, and only got worse as he got older 


control, education, science and technology. 

For those who survived attacks by the 
Unabomber, the prospect of a trial evokes 
feelings ranging from dread to relief. Uni- 
versity of Colorado engineering professor 
John Hauser, who was an Air Force pilot and 
aspiring astronaut when he was injured in a 
May 1985 bombing at Berkeley, says the ar- 
rest of a suspect and the halt to the bombings 
meant more to him than the trial. “If having 
the trial over means that I could fly jets again 
and pursue those paths, Id say, “Hey, great! 
Cool!” he told Time. “But it’s not going to 
bring my hand back or the use of my arm. So 
the trial doesn’t matter all that much. I'm not 
going to regain what I’ve lost.” |

Theodore Kaczynski’s remote Montana cabin — his 
wilderness hideaway from the modern world — may 
save his life at his upcoming trial. 
Legal analysts say the stark, plywood cabin and its 
200 books, old newspaper clippings, and scattered odds 
and ends will humanize the Unabomber defendant and 


may help convince a jury to 
spare him from the death 
| | Penalty.

Lydia Eccles interviews Criminal lawyer Michael Mello, Vermont Law School 


NB: Over the summer, Judge Burrell had denied a defense motion to exclude Ted’s diaries. Attorney Michael Mello 
published a newspaper op-ed piece, Ted Kaczynski’s Diary, arguing that diaries are inadmissible evidence because 
they are self-incrimination. Lydia went to Vermont Law School to interview him. Mike was broadly experienced with 
death penalty cases and he knew Ted’s attorneys. The timing was perfect, because the trial soon erupted. 


“Mike became our ally, and directly appealed for Ted’s rights through Unapack’s website as the trial unfolded, 
writing urgent pieces in a single afternoon to be uploaded to the website. CNN, the Sacramento Bee and other 
media linked to Unapack’s site. He was the only legal expert to passionately and publicly speak up for Ted’s rights 
at trial."—Lydia Eccles 


THE NEW YORK TIMES NATIONAL WEDNESDAY, NOVEMBER 26, 1997 


Angry Unabom Defendant Hurls His Pen Over Discussion of His Sanity 


By WILLIAM GLABERSON 


SACRAMENTO, Calif., Nov. 25 — 
Theodore J. Kaczynski threw his pen 


across the defense table today as . 


lawyers debated his refusal to be 
examined by Government psychia- 
trists. 

The show of emotion was the most 
demonstrative yet from Mr. Kaczyn- 
ski, who typically seems unmoved by 
even the most negative comments 
about him. 

Jury selection is under way here 
for Mr. Kaczynski’s trial on charges 
that he was the Unabomber responsi- 
ble for three deaths and more than 
two dozen injuries in an 18-year cam- 
paign of package bombings. 

The legal arguments today c 
cerned negotiations between defense 

-and prosecution lawyers on whether 
they could agree to testing of Mr. 


»cezynski, 


Kaczynski by prosecution experts. 
The judge in the case, Garland E. 
Burrell Jr. of Federal District Court 
here, ordered the talks last week 
when he.began considering a pros- 
ecution motion to bar Mr. Kaczyn- 
ski’s lawyers from asserting a men- 
tal-illness defense because he has 
refused to be examined by prosecu- 
tion psychiat: 

With a great deal of evidence im- 
plicating Mr. Kaczynski, his effort to 
use a psychiatric defense has be- 
come a central issue in the case. 

In reporting to the judge on the 
talks today, the chief prosecutor, 
Robert J. Cleary, said the Govern- 
ment had proposed five options for 
psychiatric examination of Mr. Ka- 
including personal inter- 
views for a limited time and written 
questions. Mr. Cleary said the de- 


Lawyers debate how 
to handle someone 
who refuses to talk to 
psychiatrists. 


fense had rejected those offers. 

Mr. Cleary said the prosecutors 
had told defense lawyers of one ex- 
amination their experts wanted to 
conduct, the Minnesota Multiphasic 
Personality Inventory, but had not 
specified additional types of exami- 
nations because Mr. Kaczynski’s 
lawyers had not said whether he 
would subject himself to any neuro- 
logical examination. 


The defense has argued that the 
Government may not need additional 
neurological examinations because 
prosecution experts could simply in- 
terpret results of neurological test- 
ing done by the defense. A defense 
psychologist says her testing showed 
brain abnormalities consistent with 
paranoid schizophrenia. 

A defense lawyer, Gary D. 
Sowards, said that because Mr. 
Cleary had not specified what neuro- 
logical examinations it wished to 
conduct, the defense lawyers could 
not respond. Mr. Sowards said the 
defense was ing to formulate a 
proposal to make to Mr. Kaczynski. 

In his remarks. to the judge, Mr. 
Cleary said it was up to the defense 
to respond to the Government re- 
quest. The prosecutor described Mr. 
Kaczynski’s refusal several weeks 


ago to follow an order by Judge Bur- 4 
rell to submit to psychiatric testing } 
“a violation of the most blatant sort” | 
that may deprive the Government of 
“what may be the most important 
evidence in this case.” 

Mr. Sowards said the raw neuro- 
logical tests conducted by defense ff 
experts could be compared to X-rays 
that could be interpreted equally by 
both sides. 

“Ts there something wrong with 
our X-rays?”’ Mr. Sowards asked Mr. 
Cleary in the courtroom. “If there is, 
what test would you like to do?”’ 

It was at that point that Mr. Ka- 
ezynski, whose lawyers say he denies 
any mental impairment, grew agitat- 
ed. But it was not clear whether he 
was angry at the Government or at 
his own lawyers for saying that the 
tests prove he is mentally ill.

SATURDAY, DECEMBER 27, 1997 


Drug Cases 


Are Upended 
By the Police 
In Chicago 


By DIRK JOHNSON 


CHICAGO, Dec. 26 — In this city 
famous for regarding the law as a 
|dare, the hustle can reach the level of 
_art form. Now comes a Chicago-style 
way for suspects to beat the rap: get 
hooked by police officers who may 
not be so pure themselves. 

In the fallout of a police scandal a 
year ago in which officers extorted 
and robbed undercover officers pos- 
ing drug dealers, the Cook County 
State’s Attorney’s office has dropped 
124 narcotics cases involving the ac- 
‘cused officers in the last year. 

“When you take away the main 
'witness, you don’t have much of a 
case,” said Robert Benjamin, a 
spokesman for the prosecutor’s  of- 
fice. ‘These police officers would not 
exactly have made the best witnéss- 
es, under the circumstances, and we 
|were not eager to have them testify.”’ 
| Besides that, Mr. Benjamin said, 
lawyers for the accused officers 
‘would not let their clients testify in 
court, thus shooting a rather large 
hole in a criminal case. 

Seven Chicago police officers in 
the crime-ridden Austin District 
jwere indicted a year ago for taking 
'$65,000 from people they thought 
were drug dealers but were actually 
undercover officers. Prosecutors say 
video cameras were rolling during 
some of these business deals. 
| One of the Austin officers has 
pleaded guilty to robbing an utder- 
cover officer posing as a drug dealer. 
The other six officers have pleaded 
hot guilty and are expected to go to 
fa) in March. 

The Austin scandal cost progecu- 
ors 120 cases. A scandal in the 
resham District, in which three of- 

icers on Monday were found guilty 
f robbing undercover officers pos- - 
ng as drug dealers, pai if j 
ere forced to drop four cases. 
No more charges will be drop 
S a result of the scandals, Mr. 
amin said, adding: ‘‘It’s over. We 
lushed them out of the system,’””

Freeway 
overhaul 
sneaks up 
on S.F. 


‘Nightmare’ project 
to block Bay Bridge 
ramps, close streets 


By Gerald D. Adams 
EXAMINER URBAN PLANNING WRITER 


In a plan certain to affect thou- 
sands of motorists, state highway 
officials are preparing to launch a 
little-known public works project 
that for five years will close two 
downtown San Francisco streets to 
traffic and at various times block 
several ramps to the Bay Bridge. 

The $200 million project to ret- 
rofit the western Bay Bridge ap- 
proach will begin in 1999 and last 
for five years, overlapping the 
planned opening of the nearby Gi- 
ants baseball park in April 2000. 

“For five years this is going to be 
the nightmare of nightmares,” said. 


ski and his lawyers. Several hours 
later, the judge announced there 
would be no opening statements 
until Thursday. He sent the jurors 
home until then. 

The developments Monday, 
coupled with a series of legal ma- 
neuvers in days leading up to the 
trial, have renewed speculation 
that Kaczynski’s conflicts with his 
attorneys threaten to unravel his 
defense. 

Legal observers say closed-door 
meetings between the judge, the 
defendant and his defense team 
typically involve attorney-client is- 
sues. 

Kaczynski, who could face the 
death penalty if convicted of two 
fatal bombings, met twice with the 
judge last month in an attempt to 
dismiss his lawyers. He apparently 
had a dispute over the mental de- 
fect defense his attorneys were 
planning to pursue during trial. 

Public defenders Quin Denvir 
and Judy Clarke, who contend that 
Kaczynski is a paranoid schizo- 
phrenic, eventually dropped plans 
for a defense based on his mental 
state. 

Kaczynski is considered compe- 
tent to stand trial in federal court. 
That means he is allowed to dictate 
his own defense. 

The 55-year-old former mathe- 
matics professor, who lived in a. 
tiny Montana shack, has stubborn- 
ly resisted suggestions that he has 
mental problems. 

He has refused to be examined 
by government psychiatrists — un- 
dermining his attorneys’ ability to 
argue that he had a mental defect 
and squashing what for months 
was expected to be the basis of his 
defense. 1B 

Using a variation of the dimin- 
ished capacity defense, Kaczyn- 
ski’s lawyers had intended to argue 
that he was incapable of the crimi- 
nal intent necessary to be found 
guilty. 

“It’s a nightmare,” said Mal- 
colm Segal, a defense attorney and 
former federal prosecutor in Sacra- 
mento. “They can’t introduce evi- 
dence against his will, even if they 
think it’s in his best interest.” 

Seated in the courtroom Mon- 
day were two men injured in Una- 
bomber attacks: David Gelertner, 
the Yale professor who lost several 
fingers in a bomb attack, and 
Charles Epstein, a geneticist at 
UC-San Francisco. 

Also present were family mem- 
bers of two men killed by bombs: 
timber lobbyist Gilbert Murray 
and computer store owner Hugh 
Scrutton. 

Murray’s widow and son were 
seated in the front row, as were 
Kaczynski’s mother, Wanda Kac- 


Unabom Tria

said rulings both about the refusal to

limiting Mr. Kaczynski’s right to

irts wide discretion about last- 
inute requests for delay. But the 
on the question of whether a

fense is not well defined.

letter from Mr. Serra. He has sug- 
gested that he might argue that Mr.

his anti-technology campaign to, ulti-

Ravage supports Unabomber! 


We like to express our support to mister Ted Kaczinsky. His life story as 

well as the Freedom Club's manifesto have our uttermost interest. Being one 

of Holland's well-known political-cultural magazines, Ravage is leftist but 

not correct. To us, the ideas expressed in the manifesto 'Industrial Society 

and its Consequences' have to be taken seriously by everyone who cares about 

the future of our planet and the quality of our daily lives. Therefore we 

pity the dubious case against mr. Kaczinsky: all attention is drawn towards 

him personally instead of the ideas which concern everybody, not only in the 
United States but all across the industrialized world. Whether mr. Kaczinsky 

MORE (you've seen 59%):is the Unabomber or not, the ideas show that time's almost 
need to fight for drastic changes, or else human life will disappear in short Ue 
time. Ravage is happy that mr. Kaczinsky gains so widespread support from all i 
kinds of different people. We'd like to encourage all of you to go on with 

your struggle. 


Ravage, two-weekley action-magazine

Subject: Re: STOP THIS TRIAL! KACZYNSKI IS BEING DENIED HIS RIGHTS (fwd) 
To: rcole@ap.org (R Cole) 
Date: Fri, 9 Jan 1998 20:51:17 -0600 (CST) 


Dear Richard: 


I just e-mailed you our press release of yesterday. We consider this 
situation a crisis, and our priority is to put word out that the trial 
should be stopped, and there should be a delay for either a new 
lawyer--specifically Tony Serra, who is willing to do a necessity 
defense--or for Judy Clark to prepare to represent her client according to 
his wishes. That he should be left with no alternative but to represent 
himself would be an outrageous travesty of justice, all the more so ina 
capital case. 


I am unhappy that the media seems to be accepting the notion that Ted 
changed his mind at the eleventh hour. How do you know this? 

He has been quarantined for a year and a half. Did Ted EVER consent to an 
insanity defense? Given how he is expressing himself now, do you think 
that he did? Remember that there were various motions to suppress, plea 
bargain negotiations, etc. Another question: When did Ted first attempt 
MORE (you've seen 26%):to contact Serra or seek outside assistance, i.e. Chris 
is the history of this rift? Is it true that he 

is too late and changing his mind? Or has he been unable to act, given 
the powerlessness of his situation? I hope that you will scrutinize that. 
It is all to easy to continue seeing each act of resistance on his part as 
more signs of mental illness. 


I am bringing these things up because time is of the essence here, and if 
it is NOT true that Ted suddenly changed his mind on the first day of 
trial--this completely goes to whether it is legitimate for him to have a 
chance to start over with lawyers that are open with him and respect his 
wishes. To put it bluntly, I feel that he is being fucked by his lawyers. 
Thus he is now totally isolated and there is NO one to represent him -- 
and he is helpless, because he is imprisoned, and cannot even write his 
own visitors list. 


I realize I am reading alot into this, but I am very concerned that the 
media is not doing its job and taking a skeptical attitude towrard the 
proceedings and toward the defense lawyers. Particularly since the issue 
concerns silencing the political expression of someone who may have risked 
his life to voice his political concerns, concerns that he devoted his 
life to also in the way he lived, the things he sacrificed, and years of 
study and thought. 

MORE (you've seen 63%): 

We already know that he is not a master of social process/negotioation, 
etc. He has been living in isolation for years. To come out that and try 
to deal with the social aspects of being pressured and cajoled by some of 
the most competent lawyers in the country, etc.??? 


I think the media could play a critical role in preventing him from being 


railraoded if they, i.e. you were to try to shed some light on the history 
of this situation, and when and how the rift came about. 


Lydia

PRESS RELEASE (COMMENTARY) __!'V SAC BEE 

UNAPACK: THE UNABOMBER POLITICAL ACTION COMMITTEE vee 

HTTP: WWW.PARANOIA.COM/UNAPACK/ E-MAIL: UNAPACK@PARANOIA.COM _ i 8] 
(> LIDIA EecrES ) 

FOR IMMEDIATE RELEASE: JANUARY 15, 1998 Po Box 120 ¥GY 

Contact: Michael Mello 1-802-763-8303 X2291 BOSIOWU, MA OWI2 


. 
REPRESENTING TED KACZYNSKI: FSA 
THE RIGHT TO ASSISTANCE OF COUNSEL //\45< 
GP The wtmdn T Spoke ts Oo 
i The plume: pleace wrte tf You 
By Michael Mello Pies & dk gas on “te 
Pcs anes , Mading List — “er 
Theodore Kaczynski is being denied his day in court: Lawyers he does not want are forcing him to stake 
his life on a defense he would rather die than raise. In the guise of providing him with his Constitutional 
right to the assistance of counsel--"assistance" is the word used in the Sixth Amendment --the federal 
government has stripped him of the only power he has left as an American citizen: the power to have his 
case raised against the indictment, to put on his defense in a judicial proceeding where his life is on the 
line-- --not his lawyer's life, not his judge's life. 


Judge Burrell ruled last week that Kaczynski cannot fire his lawyers and that those lawyers can raise a 
defense based on Kaczynski's alleged mental illness--a defense that Kaczynski adamantly refuses. 
Kaczynski wants a "necessity defense"--a claim that his crimes were justified as part of his political war 
against technology on behalf of humanity. Federal law would likely preclude such a defense to the murder 
charges, and Kaczynski and his lawyers appear to recognize that he will almost certainly be found guilty 
of murder at the first phase of his bifurcated capital trial. The real battleground in United States v. 
Kaczynski is over penalty. And at the penalty phase of the trial, Kaczynski's "necessity defense" evidence 
is admissible, in my view, under the Supreme Court's 1978 Lockett decision. 


Judge Burrell's rulings turn the right to assistance of counsel on its head. They transform a Constitutional 
protection designed to shield a defendant's rights into a sword that disembowels them. The whole 
purpose of the right to counsel at criminal trials--a right recognized since the infamous Scottsboro case in 
1932--is to empower the citizen-accused. 


Ted Kaczynski's lawyers, however well-intentioned and paternalistic, are not "assisting" him. They are 
controlling him. They are strong-arming a man on trial for his life, a man the judge has already found 
mentally competent to stand trial--a ruling which means that Kaczynski is competent to make the 
important decisions in his case such as whether he will testify, whether he would accept a guilty plea, and 
whether to stake his life on a mental illness defense (a defense with little chance of success in this case). If 
Kaczynski's lawyers feel so strongly that he is too crazy to stand trial, they should have asked the judge 
months ago to explore that issue in a serious way, not with a pro forma quickie psychiatric exam. 


Now that the trial has been postponed until January 22, there is a bit of time for all sides in the case to 
step back, take a deep breath and re-assess their respective positions. The prosecutors should reconsider 
their unfortunate decision to reject a negotiated plea to life imprisonment without parole. The judge 
should sort out Kaczynski's counsel situation, once and for all, in a manner fair to Kaczynski and least 
likely to be reversed on appeal. 


Above & Opposite: 

15 January 1998 

Unapack press release, Representing Ted Kaczynski: The Right to Assistance of Counsel, Michael Mello 
NB: on the 18 January, The Sacramento Bee contacts Unapack to publish Mike Mello’s press release piece 


But the deepest soul-searching must be done by Kaczynski's court-appointed lawyers, because they are at 
least partially responsible for the disturbing events of last week. They must have known from the outset 
that their client opposed a mental illness defense. They apparently hoped that when forced--on the eve of 
his trial--to choose between going along with their defense or representing himself, Kaczynski would cave 
in. It was a gamble, and the lawyers lost. 


The hard part about playing chicken is knowing when to flinch. Ted Kaczynski didn't flinch. Left with no 
acceptable alternative, he chose to represent himself. 


I hope that Judy Clarke and Quin Denvir will now decide that they cannot ethically abandon Kaczynski to 
represent himself pro se. He clearly does not want to represent himself--and for very good reasons. He 
wants a lawyer willing to abide by his wishes. 


His lawyers themselves now face a choice: To represent Kaczynski the way he wants and has a right to be 
represented; or to step aside and allow Tony Serra (who is willing to represent Kaczynski, without fee) to 
serve as Kacyznski's lawyer. If they step aside, they should do so now--to allow Serra as much trial 
preparation time as possible. Either way, a continuance to allow time for trial preparation is absolutely 
necessary. 


The real issue here, as elsewhere in the Unabomber matter, is power. Who decides what his true interests 
are? The man whose life hangs in the balance? Or his court-appointed lawyers? 


I believe the choice is his. His superb lawyers’ job--their ethical duty as lawyers and their moral duty as 
human beings--is not to manage or control him, but to "assist" him in making his defense. 


Judge Burrell's rulings have put Judy Clarke and Quin Denvir in an ethically awkward position. They have 
acted in what they honestly believe to be their client's best /egal interests. But that is not the point. 


The Supreme Court has said repeatedly that the legality of death penalty trials must be judged by the 
"evolving standards of decency that mark the progress of a maturing society." Consider how our 
standards of decency have "evolved" from 1859 to today. 


John Brown, the slavery abolitionist who raided the federal arsenal at Harper's Ferry, Virginia in 1859, 
was critical in galvanizing public opinion so that civil war became possible--if not inevitable. John 
Brown's hanging by the Commonwealth of Virginia made him a celebrated martyr in the North, 
convincing the South that compromise on the slavery issue was impossible and so that secession (and 
war) were the only course--exactly as Brown himself had hoped and planned. 


Perhaps the most striking aspect of John Brown--besides the subsequent vindication of his "crazy" 
abolitionist views--was his carriage during his trial and the way his lawyers respected him. At trial, Brown 
refused to allow his lawyers to raise an insanity defense (Brown's family had a history of insanity). Brown 
knew exactly what he was doing when he raided Harper's Ferry: attempting to incite a slave rebellion, a 
plan far-fetched but certainly not crazy (at least not to Virginia and the South, in the years following Nat 
Turner, Denmark Vesey and Gabriel Prosser rebellions and other slave uprisings). If Brown was crazy, 
then so were a number of prominent northern abolitionists. And, like Socrates, after Brown's trial and 
death sentence, he categorically scotched the plans of his followers to organize Brown's escape from 
Virginia. No, Brown insisted: His execution would do more for his cause than anything he could ever do 
alive. On this score, Brown was absolutely right, at least in the eyes of historians. Our standards of 


01/16/98 08: 


decency have come a long way in 139 years. But on one point they remain unchanged: Some things are 
worth dying for. 


In a column in last week's Boston Globe, Ellen Goodman asked rhetorically whether "the Mad Hatter" 
should be "running the show" in the Sacramento courtroom. My answer is, hell, yes! When he's on trial 
for his life, it's his show to run...with assistance of counsel, according to his right under the Sixth 
Amendment to the United States Constitution. 


Michael Mello is a professor of ethics at Vermont Law School who, as a capital appellate public defender 
in Florida (1983-86), represented many death row prisoners, including one would-be political martyr -- 
Paul Hill. He is co-author, with Paul Perkins, of a law review article, 7D KACZYSNKIT'S DIARIES, 
which argues that admission of Kaczynski's personal diaries constitutes unconstitutionally compelled 
self-incrimination, under the 1886 landmark Supreme Court case, Boyd v. United States. His memoir, 
Dead Wrong: A Death Row Lawyer Speaks Out Against Capital Punishment, was recently published by 
the University of Wisconsin Press. He can be reached at Vermont Law School, South Royalton, Vermont 
05068 (802)763-8303 X2291. 


Unapack (The Unabomber Political Action Committee) assisted in the conception of this statement of 
opposition to the legal coercion of Theodore Kaczynski. Much appreciation to Michael Mello!

been “in coritact with him by

CRIMINAL LAW BULLETIN 


new lawyers might find a persuasive precedent in the 1859 story of 
John Brown and his trial lawyers. 


Epilogue: Ted Kaczynski Speaks for Himself 


On July 7, 1998, after this essay had been typeset, I learned that a 
theretofore confidential statementJby Theodore Kaczynski—setting out 
his views on his battles with his lawyers—had recently been published 
1n thefperiodical Live Wild or Die, in Berkeley, California. 


The statement reads as follows: 


INFORMATION CONCERNI?'G THE CASE OF THEODORE J. 
KACZYNSKI, ACCUSED OF BEIN ~ THE UNABOMBER. 


Fer a matter of months preceding the beginning of my trial on November 12, 
(997, Lhad been aware that my attorneys wanted to use a defense that would 
be based in part on supposed evidence of mental impairment. However, my 
attorneys have led me to believe that I would have a considerable measure of 
control over the defense strategy, hence ] was under the impression that I 
would be able to limit the presentation of mental evidence to some items 
that at the time I thought might have some validity. 

The first weeks of the trial were devoted to selection of a jury, a process 
that told me little about the defense that my attorneys planned to use. But in 
late November I discovered that my attorneys had prepared a defense that 
would virtually portray me as insane, and that they were going to force this 
defense on me in spite of my bitter resistance to it. 

For the present I will not review in detail what happened between late 
November, 1997 and January 22, 1998. Suffice it to say that the judge in my 
case, Garland E. Burrell, decided that my attorneys had the legal right to 
force their defense on me over my objections; that it was too late for me to 
replace my attorneys with a certain distinguished attorney who had offered 
to represent me and had stated his intention to use a defense not based on 
any supposed mental illness; and that it was too late for me to demand the 
right to act as my own attorney. 

This put me in such a position that I had only one way left to prevent my 
attorneys from using false information to represent me to the world as insane: 
I agreed to plead guilty to the charges in exchange for withdrawal of the 
prosecution’s request for the death penalty. I also had to give up all right to 
appeal, which leaves me with a virtual certainty of spending my life in prison. 
I am not afraid of the death penalty, and I agreed to this bargain only to end 
the trial and thus prevent my attorneys from representing me as insane. It 
should be noted that the defense my attorneys had planned could not have 
Jed to my release; it was only intended to save me from the death penalty. 

By concealing their intentions from me and discouraging me from finding 
another attorney before it was too late, my attorneys have done me very 


326 


Above & Opposite: 

26 January 1998 

Last pages of USA v. Theodore John Kaczynski: One of the Most Famous Non-Trials in History by 
Michael Mello, Criminal Law Bulletin, with his handwritten notes 


RAISING HOLY HELL 


great harm: They have forced me to sacrifice my right to an appeal that 
might have led to my release; they have also ready made public the opinions 
of supposed experts who portray me as crazy; and they have caused me to 
lose my opportunity to be represented by a distinguished attorney who would 
have portrayed me in a very different light. 

Perhaps I ought to hate my attorneys for what they have done to me, but 
I do not. Their motives were in no way malicious. They are essentially 
conventional people who are blind to some of the implications of this case, 
and they acted as they did because they subscribe to certain professional 
principles that they believe left them no alternative. These principles may 
seem rigid and even ruthless to a non-lawyer, but there is no doubt that my 
attorneys believe in them sincerely. Moreover, on a personal level my 
attorneys have treated me with great generosity and have performed many 
kindnesses for me. (But these can never compensate for the harm they have 
done me through their handling of my case.) 

Recent events constitute a major defeat for me. But the end is not yet. 


More will be heard from me in the future. 
Theodore J. Kaczynski 2. of | 
January 26, 1998

BENVENUTO CELLINI was born in Florence in the year 1500, where 
he spent the early years of his life training to be a goldsmith. With his 
love of beauty -- especially the beauty of the human form -- went a 
delight in craftsmanship and difficult achievement. Even his liking for 
warfare was a delight in dramatic execution and skillful effect. His 
"Life" has taken its place as the most notorious of all autobiographies.

5 October 2020 
Letter from Ted Kaczynski to Lydia Eccles 


Previous: 
April 1999 
Lydia Eccles, Notecard for Ted Kaczynski at Florence Supermax, Florence, Colorado 


December 18, 2022 [sending late as usual] 
Dear Ted, 


I recently came across this long forgotten picture of me in my loft space taken in 1993, taken 
when I was working on a first amendment lawsuit brief against the subway system to prevent 
them from installing loads of advertising televisions in the subway station. I was working with 
my collaborator Wendy; we saw this state-sponsored system as a good chance to talk about ad- 
vertising in general as diffuse propaganda; we had a lots of fun torturing the subway system with 
a myriad stickers satirizing “progress” under the project name, “You're Soaking In It!” You can 
see the obvious pink, black and white reason I got excited about ISAAF when I got hold of that 
New York Times insert!!! 


While many of your predictions are coming to pass, I am glad that you were wrong last Decem- 
ber about not making to another Christmas. I hope for still another Christmas, at least, and that 
your writing and support network will be harmonious and productive in 2023... let me know if 
you want a book. 

Love from Lydia [P.S. I am also sending you the card I made for Betsy this year.] 


Cloristwvis cud @ Happy Mew (edu 


Above: 

18 December 2022 

Letter from Lydia Eccles to Ted Kaczynski 

NB: Ted Kaczynski was diagnosed with cancer in December 2021. He was moved to the Federal Medical 
Center in Butner, North Carolina, for treatment. A notecard with his new address soon followed 


THEODORE J. KACZYNSKI, 1942-2023 


A Lonely Boy Genius Became 
A Terrorist as the ‘Unabomber’ 


ELAINE THON : ASSOCIATED PRESS 
Theodore Kaczynski in 1996. 
He died Saturday in prison. 


JOKES ABOUT BOMBS WILL NOT BE TAKEN LIGHTLY. 
1995 ?T eUnabomber M anifesto 2025 ! 


Presented by Universal Aliens Salvage Ethnography 
Lydia Eccles/Test Human Participant-O bserver 


Published April, 2025 
First Edition of 60 copies 
Printed in Italy 


All artworks/texts by Lydia Eccles, unless otherwise stated 
All images provided by Lydia Eccles 

All press & photos scanned by Lydia Eccles 

Courtesy the artist 


T is edition, 2025 Road House 
Published by Road House 


Designed by Lydia Eccles & Ruiz Stephinson 
Edited by Ruiz Stephinson 
www.goswellroad.com 


Theodore J. Kaczynski, the so- 
called Unabomber, who attacked 
academics, businessmen and ran- 
dom civilians with homemade 
bombs from 1978 to 1995, killing 
three people and injuring 23 with 
the stated goal of fomenting the 
collapse of the modern social or- 
der — a violent spree that ended 
after what was often described as 
the longest and most costly man- 
hunt in American history — died 
on Saturday in a federal prison 
medical center in Butner, N.C. He 
was 81. 

A spokesman for the Federal 
Bureau of Prisons said Mr. Ka- 
czynski was found unresponsive 
in his cell early in the morning. 
The bureau did not specify a 
cause, but three people familiar 
with the situation said he died by 
suicide. 

The bureau had announced his 
transfer to the medical facility in 
2021. 

Mr. Kaczynski traced a singular 
path in American life: lonely boy 
genius to Harvard-trained star of 
pure mathematics, to rural rec- 
luse, to notorious murderer, to im- 
prisoned extremist. 

In the public eye, he fused two 
styles of violence: the periodic 
targeting of the demented serial 
killer, and the ideological fanati- 
cism of the terrorist. 

After he was captured by about 
40 EB.I. agents in April 1996, Mr. 
Kaczynski’s particular ideology 
was less the subject of debate than 
the question of whether his crimes 
should be dignified with a rational 
motive to begin with. 

Victims railed against commen- 
tators who took seriously a 
35,000-word manifesto that he 
had written to justify his actions 
and evangelize the ideas that he

Opposite: 
Spring 1982 


Charles Black, The Shouting of a Huge Belief 

NB: This was given to Lydia Eccles and Wendy Hamer by Charles Black in 1993 as they sued the subway 
system. He had sued the Washington, D.C. bus system for imposing Muzak on a captive audience in 1952. 
He went on to argue a landmard desegregation case before the U.S. Supreme Court 


The Shouting of a Huge Behef 


CHARLES BLACK wy 


The shouting of a huge belief 
Bounces on chalk hills, big enough 
To command the assent of coyotes. 


_ For any sized-down belief 


In this’ sad-sounding city, - | 
There is only a little breathing-room; 


Tiny Juminous creeds 
Are too thin, they shatter 
Under mounting city sorrow. 


But the immense chalk hills 


Throw back, again and again and again, 
A huge belief from vastly gone ages.
